Current Affairs Commentary

The Issue of Banning Oil Shipments to Italy

— Ang

Mussolini's expedition to East Africa, although not stopped by the League of Nations' sanctions, has clearly faced significant difficulties as a result. The Committee of Eighteen is scheduled to meet again on the 12th of this month to vote on the date for banning oil shipments to Italy. The British cabinet has decided to participate after a three-hour cabinet meeting. It is heard that the French government has also reached an understanding with Britain. If Mussolini still refuses to comply, then the ban on oil and other similar severe plans will be gradually implemented in the very short term. This poses a very serious threat to Italy, which is poor in resources.

According to the League of Nations' further sanctions plans, the first to be banned from being shipped to Italy are kerosene and gasoline, followed by major products such as copper, iron, coal, and cotton. These are raw materials necessary for industry in peacetime and the driving force of mechanized armies in wartime, all of which Italy lacks. For example, nine-thirds of the oil burned is supplied by the United States and Romania, while coal depends entirely on supplies from Britain and Germany. Once the source is cut off, the stagnation of industry is a given, and in terms of military affairs, the operation of aircraft and the transportation of ships will lose their flexibility due to the lack of fuel. In view of the crisis ahead, Mussolini decided a few days ago to establish a state-run metal mining bureau to be responsible for the exploitation of domestic mines and ordered gas plants and coal mines to maximize production. There is also a plan to use alcohol as a substitute for fuel, which is enough to reveal his awkward predicament.

The ban on oil was originally based on a motion by the Canadian representative, but the Canadian government suddenly announced yesterday that its representative's proposal was not representative of the government's opinion. This is not surprising. In the British Empire, Canada's policies have always been known for their stability. Throughout history, collective security movements such as the 1922 Mutual Assistance Treaty and the 1924 Geneva Protocol have failed due to Canada's opposition. At the first session of the League of Nations, the Canadian representative said, "In this group of mutual insurance, the responsibilities of each country are quite unequal. Our situation is certainly not combustible, and we are very far from the flammable materials." It seems unwilling to assume more obligations for international security. Canada has always followed this principle in its attitude towards international issues. The denial of its representative's remarks in Geneva this time has not violated its consistent spirit. Moreover, according to yesterday's telegram, the Canadian government will still support sanctions against Italy, so it can be seen that this matter has not had a major impact on the progress of the sanctions policy.

However, the effectiveness of this sanction still depends on the degree of cooperation of various countries. Judging from the current situation, the United States, which is in an important position, although not a member of the League of Nations and bound by its own neutrality law, its Interior Minister Ickes has first advised exporters to stop selling oil to Italy. Secretary of State Hull recently reiterated that it is also possible that US cotton will not be exported to warring countries. Other major oil-producing countries, such as Romania, seem to be hesitant, but are also prepared to follow the united action of various countries. Iraq is only looking to Britain for guidance. The Soviet Union and Iran are even more obviously in favor of further sanctions. Therefore, the cooperation of various countries is unlikely to encounter any problems.

Resolving the Italian-Abyssinian Dispute: The Atmosphere of Peace Talks Intensifies; Smooth Discussions Between British and French Experts; Hoare to Meet with Laval

(London) According to news from Paris, discussions between British and French experts aimed at resolving the Italian-Abyssinian War are proceeding very smoothly. It is heard that the differences of opinion between the two countries are not fundamental. The experts may complete their work in a matter of days. It is widely believed that they did not discuss plans involving the cession of land to Italy, but only discussed the details of the suggestions made by the former League of Nations Committee of Five, which would grant Italy significant economic benefits in Abyssinia and the southern province of Ogaden. French Prime Minister Laval is keeping the Italian Ambassador to France, Cerruti, informed of the progress of the talks, which is noteworthy. (Reuters, 4th)

(Paris) News from here today indicates that Britain and France have decided to offer Italy further peace terms before implementing the oil embargo. The plan will still be based on the proposals rejected by Mussolini in mid-August, namely, placing Abyssinia under League of Nations trusteeship, with Italy assuming the greatest responsibility for the trusteeship. In addition, there is a proposed land swap between Italy and Abyssinia to provide Abyssinia with a sea outlet. It is claimed that Mussolini is willing to study this solution. As for the plan itself, it has not yet been formally drafted, but today the atmosphere surrounding the situation in Europe has become noticeably more optimistic. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Paris) According to a London dispatch received by Le Matin, British Foreign Secretary Sir Samuel Hoare will arrive in France from London this Saturday to meet with Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval. During the meeting, he will present Laval with several proposals that are very helpful in quickly resolving the Italian-Abyssinian dispute and will bring the opinions of Britain and France into complete harmony. (Havas, 4th)

British and French Views Increasingly Converge

(London) Foreign Secretary Sir Samuel Hoare will travel to Switzerland at the end of this week for a few days of rest and will arrive in Paris on Saturday to hold talks with French Prime Minister Laval. According to sources at our agency, the solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute drafted by British and French experts will be jointly discussed by Hoare and Laval. Regarding this solution, the opinions of Britain and France are now increasingly converging. It is heard that the two countries have agreed to divide Abyssinian territory into two parts: the core area and the non-Amharic areas, with the non-Amharic areas coming under Italian control. However, Britain and France still find it difficult to agree on the extent of control. Britain argues that while Italy can participate in the administration of the area, its sovereignty should still be held by the Emperor of Abyssinia. Italy's territorial claims in the Tigray Province can also be satisfied, but in exchange for Abyssinia gaining an outlet to the Red Sea. It is generally believed that this plan will not be acceptable to either Mussolini or the Abyssinian Emperor. (Havas, 3rd)

Rome Feels a Sense of Relief

(Rome) According to our agency's diplomatic correspondent, political circles here only began to feel a sense of relief yesterday regarding the solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. This is because unofficial news from Paris suggests that the talks between British Foreign Office expert on Abyssinian affairs, Mr. Patteson, and the head of the African Department of the French Foreign Ministry, Mr. Saint-Quentin, and other experts, are sufficient to produce a proposal for resolving the dispute that is acceptable to Italy. Regarding the solution to the dispute, Italy's view is that the northern province of Tigray should not be abandoned, as it has been occupied by Italian forces. The people of that province are wholeheartedly devoted to the Italian side, and their voluntary surrender sometimes precedes the arrival of Italian troops. Some villagers have even come to pledge allegiance before the arrival of Italian troops. If Italian troops were to withdraw, the Abyssinian government would implement retaliatory measures. To abandon the people of that province would be a dereliction of duty. As for Italian Somaliland, officials here believe that the Paris experts' talks must have touched on the demarcation of the boundary between Italian Somaliland and the southern regions of Abyssinia. The new boundary line will be changed from an oblique line from northeast to southwest to a straight line from north to south. Specialists in colonial administration are closely monitoring developments in this area, as the mountainous terrain there is easy to develop and is of utmost importance. In short, as of now, the news from Paris to Rome, although unofficial, is largely encouraging and has dispelled the gloomy atmosphere. (Havas, 4th)

Widespread Rumors of Italy and the US Reaching an Oil Agreement; Rome and US Oil Companies Deny It; US Political Authorities Unwilling to Comment

(Rome) Today, the Associated Press learned from reliable sources that the Italian government has reached a "gentleman's agreement" with the Italian-American Oil Company, a branch of Standard Oil of New Jersey (Esso), to cope with the League of Nations' oil embargo against Italy. If the League of Nations Sanctions Committee passes the embargo, the Italian-American Oil Company will supply as much oil as possible to Italy in exchange for a 30-year monopoly on the Italian oil market. All oil will be supplied from Esso oil wells outside the United States, with the largest source being Romania, transported to Italy via Hungary, in order to avoid violating the US government's neutrality policy. The agreement also stipulates that Italian Eritrea can be supplied directly from the Far East, thus avoiding the Suez Canal controlled by Britain. This plan has guaranteed that the oil supply to the Italian forces in East Africa will never be depleted. It has also been learned here that Esso has agreed to extend a loan of 1 billion lire to Italy so that Italy can purchase oil with the loan. Once the League of Nations passes the oil embargo, this agreement will take effect. It is expected that this news will be denied by officials and related parties, but after a thorough investigation of three days, the Associated Press is convinced that it is reliable. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Rome) An official statement today declared that the Associated Press's report that Italy has entered into a contract with the Italian-American Oil Company is completely unfounded. (National News Agency, 4th)

(Washington) News from Rome that the Italian government has reached an oil agreement with Esso has caused great shock here. State Department officials are paying close attention to this news but are unwilling to comment. They maintain that the US government's policy has nothing to do with the League of Nations and that its sole purpose is to keep the United States out of war. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(New York) Walter Teagle, chairman of Standard Oil of New Jersey, today completely denied the Rome news that the company had reached an agreement with the Italian government to lend oil. Teagle said that this agreement would be impossible to fulfill and called it "a ridiculous piece of propaganda." He claimed that to his knowledge, the company's Italian branch has not received any proposal for such an agreement because "the authorities of the company in that region know that such a contract is absolutely unacceptable to this company." (National News Agency, 3rd)

(Geneva) International circles here regard the rumors of the Italian government reaching an agreement with Esso as "a deception." If it were true, the parties involved would not allow the details of the agreement to be leaked before the League of Nations implements the oil embargo. Diplomats said that if Romania imports oil into Italy via Hungary, the League of Nations can quickly prevent it. (National News Agency, 3rd)

(London) Observers familiar with the situation here do not believe the Rome rumors of an oil agreement because Romania has already expressed its willingness to participate in the oil embargo against Italy, and the Iranian government will prohibit the export of oil owned by American companies. (National News Agency, 3rd)

Canada Disapproves of the Oil Embargo

(Rome) According to responsible sources in Rome, the move to embargo oil to Italy will be abandoned because the Canadian government does not approve of its representative in Geneva proposing this motion. At the same time, the French Ambassador to Rome had a long conversation with Italian Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Suvich yesterday. It is heard that the French Ambassador asked Suvich to present proposals for resolving the dispute with Abyssinia, but Suvich has not yet taken action. (Reuters, 4th)

Hungary Suffers from Sanctions Against Italy

Budapest, Hungary: Hungarian Minister of Commerce de Wynckler recently told a Havas reporter, "The situation created by the implementation of sanctions against Italy by various countries is not only of no benefit to the Hungarian national economy, but has so far produced harmful results. The export of Hungarian livestock to Italy is critical to the lifeblood of the Hungarian economy. Although Hungary can continue to export as usual because it is not participating in the sanctions, Hungarian exports are still inevitably reduced because Italy restricts meat consumption, and there is no profit to be made. A large amount of Hungarian meat is currently stored in Italy and has not yet been sold." (Havas, 3rd)

Hull Issues Another Warning to Domestic Arms Dealers; Orders Registration; Criminal Prosecution for Violations; Secretary of the Interior Expresses Unwillingness to Ban Oil to Italy

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull today sternly warned all businesses and individuals engaged in the arms trade who have not yet registered in accordance with the Neutrality Act. Hull hopes that their failure to register is due to negligence but said that violators will be subject to criminal prosecution after a short deadline. (Reuters, 3rd)

(Washington) US Secretary of the Interior Ickes spoke today, changing his previous remarks in favor of banning oil exports to Italy. He said that his remarks on November 21 regarding exports to Italy and Abyssinia had been misunderstood. In fact, he only asked Americans to comply with the government's plan to stop transporting arms and wheat. The State Department did not want to comment on Ickes's remarks, but said that the government's policy of not encouraging the large-scale export of various war materials to belligerent countries has not changed to this day, but it does not want to completely ban oil exports. (Reuters, 3rd)

Italy Is Fearless in Resisting the Oil Embargo; Actively Developing Domestic Minerals; and Maximizing the Use of Alternatives

(Rome) If various countries implement an oil embargo against Italy, Italy will use two methods to resist it: one is to actively develop the minerals buried underground in the country to increase domestic oil production, and the other is to maximize the use of other fuels to replace oil. Domestic oil wells such as the Byasan diesel well produced 30,000 tons of oil last year, and active mining will naturally be carried out in the future to increase production. In addition, there are several oil wells in Sicily, Piedmont, and the Adriatic coast that will also be developed. As for alternatives to oil, according to research results, the rocks produced in Valdarno, Abruzzo, Sardinia, Umbria, Saggio di Tolando, Magella, and Marche contain lignite components, which can be used to refine oil. In addition, the marsh gas produced in Salsomaggiore can also be used as fuel. At present, most trucks and buses use carbon gas as fuel. In addition, wood alcohol and hydrogenated spirits are the best oil substitutes. The government has also taken various measures to increase alcohol production, which involves extracting alcohol from wines, grains, and beets, and then mixing this alcohol with oil to produce a new liquid fuel called "Lopol." This new fuel contains 50% oil and 48% alcohol and is currently sold throughout the country. At the same time, calcium carbide is used as automobile fuel, and the results of the experiment are very good, and the price is low and easy to popularize. In short, Italy is fearless about the oil supply, and the fact that this year's automobile race has not been stopped shows that the Italian authorities do not consider the situation after various countries impose an oil embargo to be very difficult. (Havas, 4th)

Italian Queen Donates Wedding Ring to War Effort

(Rome) The Italian Queen telegraphed Mussolini today, expressing her willingness to donate her and her husband's wedding rings to the war effort. The telegram stated that her wedding ring was the most precious of all her possessions because it would never let her forget the day she was fortunate enough to become an Italian. It is noted that the Italian Queen is Helen of Montenegro. (Reuters, 4th)

(Rome) The famous playwright Pirandello today donated the four gold medals he had won to the country to be melted down to offset sanctions expenses. One of them was attached to the Nobel Prize in Literature. (Reuters, 4th)

Japanese Naval Policy Insists on the Principle of Equality; London Conference Involves Politics; Expresses Readiness to Consider; Italian Delegation Selected

(London) A responsible Japanese official today expressed his opinion to a special Reuters naval conference reporter, saying that the basic principle of Japanese naval policy is to seek security. According to the Japanese view, this security must be achieved through the equality of the British, American, and Japanese navies and the abolition or active restriction of offensive armaments such as battleships, aircraft carriers, and 10,000-ton cruisers. Japan believes that the equality of naval power between countries can provide security because the attacker will always be at a disadvantage. Japan opposes the mutual announcement of shipbuilding procedures because it does not recognize naval equality, at least in principle. Japan will participate in this conference in a spirit of harmony. If the United States does not take a tough stance, Japan does not want to take this attitude. Japan's purpose in participating in this conference is to establish a compromise and does not want to be responsible for the breakdown of the conference. As for political issues, they are not within the scope of the instructions given to the Japanese delegation, but Japan is prepared to consider continuing Article 19 of the Washington Treaty regarding Japan and the United States not being allowed to set up defense projects on certain desert islands in the Pacific. The consideration of the 1921 Four-Power Treaty is beyond the scope of the Japanese delegation's authority. However, although the Japanese delegation has not received instructions on a Far East non-aggression pact, Japan can also approve the proposal to conclude such a pact if it is proposed at the conference. Japan advocates the abolition of submarines, but this requires the conference to issue a declaration that it will no longer build submarines, and Germany and Russia, which are not participating in the conference, should also make the same commitment. (Reuters, 4th)

(Rome) The members of the Italian delegation to the London Naval Conference have recently been decided as follows: the chief representative is the Italian Ambassador to the United Kingdom, Grandi. The other representatives are Rear Admiral Bini, Deputy Chief of Naval Staff Rear Admiral Pissia, naval experts Marcutini and Riccado Borgoni, and Lieutenant Colonel Farina. In addition, de Siris will serve as a delegation advisor, and Mr. Vitteti, counselor of the British Embassy, will also join the delegation. (Havas, 4th)

Soviet Government Plans to Raise Currency Value; Implement New Economic System

(London) It is generally believed that the Soviet Union is now preparing to implement a large number of new plans to raise currency prices and implement a new economic system. From January next year, retail prices will be reduced by 15% to 40%, and wages will also be reduced, but the rate of reduction will not be as great as the reduction in the prices of manufactured goods and food. In other words, although nominal wages will be reduced, actual wages will instead increase. In terms of production, the Soviet authorities plan to increase the average production standard of each worker, using this standard as the basis for calculating wages. The current currency will be revised to a new unit to make it a sound currency, because the progress of the Soviet gold mining industry and the sharp increase in general production have greatly improved the reserve rate of its banknotes. (Havas, 3rd)

The Historical Facts of the British, French, and Italian Rivalry in Abyssinia

— Special

Among the two major powers most closely related to Abyssinia, France is the most unassuming, occupying only a small corner in the central-eastern part of Abyssinia as its sphere of influence. However, its achievements in the economic development of Abyssinia are greater than those of any other foreign country, and it is still making progress. Abyssinia's only major industry is the 500-mile narrow-gauge railway built by the French, which runs from the port of Djibouti in the small French colony of Somaliland to the Abyssinian capital of Addis Ababa. The French have claimed that this is a clear indication that economic success can be achieved without political rule. This statement is indeed well-founded. France has been operating in Abyssinia for a century, hoping to become an important player, and it was not until this railway was built and could be profitable that it achieved complete success. The first treaty between France and Abyssinia was concluded between the French administrator Philippe and the local Abyssinian monarch Han Lasi. It was a friendly agreement that allowed the French to receive the most preferential treatment in Abyssinia and to enjoy rich commercial privileges. In fact, this agreement was of little benefit to either side, and most treaties signed with the Abyssinian king were like this.

In 1862, the French purchased a village on the shores of the Gulf of Tadjoura called Wobok for 10,000 US dollars. This gulf is located at the lower end of the Red Sea, opposite the British port of Aden, and adjacent to the Abyssinian border. They originally wanted to use this village as the center of the French colony, but later, because the land was not suitable for habitation, they found a completely new town on the opposite side of the bay called Djibouti to replace it. Thus, the builders of the French Empire did not hesitate to work hard to operate it, making it the only gateway for communication between Abyssinia and the outside world.

In 1894, a French company, relying on the influence of the French advisor to the Abyssinian Emperor Menelik's court, obtained the concession to build a railway from Djibouti across Abyssinia to the White Nile in Sudan. This was the first step in the rivalry between France and Britain to compete for possession of the central African land. At that time, Sudan and the upper reaches of the Nile were unclaimed wasteland, and the powerful could seize it at will. Everyone believed that whoever seized it first would own it. In this competition, France promised Emperor Menelik of Abyssinia to expand his territory to the Nile in order to gain Abyssinian assistance; Britain promised Italy to make all of Abyssinia the sphere of activity for Italy as a reward in order to gain Italian assistance. Britain plotted to seize Sudan, while Italy occupied part of the land of Abyssinia, which Italy later implemented.

Britain occupied Egypt in 1882, so it sent troops from the north, advancing across Egypt, and conquering Sudan along the way. Britain hoped that one army would be sent south from Cairo and another army would be sent north from the Cape of Good Hope, and that they would meet in the upper reaches of the White Nile. In this way, they could encompass the entire land spanning the African continent. However, the French army also advanced aggressively from its West African colonies and East African territories, hoping to meet in the middle and sweep across the land from west to east across the African continent, forming a whole.

When the French representative signed the Djibouti Railway Agreement in the Abyssinian capital, he dreamed that one day he would be able to board a French train on the shores of the Indian Ocean, cross the entire African continent, and get off on the shores of the Atlantic Ocean in a week or two. Britain hoped to reach Cairo from the Cape of Good Hope, and France hoped to reach the Atlantic Ocean from the Indian Ocean. Both countries entrusted capable personnel to carry out this plan. They all perked up their spirits, exhausted their intelligence, and carried out the mission of the country. They competed for a small village in central Africa called Fashoda, like a race. The prize for being the first to arrive was one million square miles of land. Lord Kitchener represented Britain, leading a large army from the north, chiseling roads when encountering dangers, building bridges when encountering water, and suppressing the fierce natives along the way. On the French side, one army was led by Captain Marchand, advancing from the west, passing through many swamps and jungles along the way. Another army was led by the Marquis de Bonchamps, advancing from the east through the canyons of the Abyssinian Plateau. At that time, it was the rainy season, and it was raining heavily. At one time, the soldiers' clothes were soaked through, causing them to shiver. Often, they used all their strength to travel only six miles a day, for several weeks. In May 18897, Bonchamps arrived in the Abyssinian capital, about 600 miles from his destination. At this time, Marchand had advanced to the upper reaches of the Ubangi River, where the river was flooding, making it difficult to cross, and there were still many extremely difficult swamps to pass ahead. Kitchener was more than 1,200 miles away, separated by three huge waterfalls and a large number of fierce enemies blocking the way. In August, the Abyssinian expedition suddenly appeared in the largest mountain range, less than 300 miles from Fashoda. Marchand had entered the Nile River basin, less than 500 miles from his destination. Kitchener was blocked by Muslims and was very far away. About a year later, the Abyssinian expedition advanced to within a day's journey of the Nile River and suddenly returned for some reason. However, another team of 10,000 Abyssinian soldiers followed closely. On June 2, 1898, the team planted the Abyssinian flag on the right bank of the Nile River a few miles above the village of Fashoda, and the French flag on the left bank. Thus, Emperor Menelik's dream of expanding the borders of his empire to the African continent was realized. Eighteen days later, Marchand led his army into Fashoda and raised the French flag. At this time, Kitchener was still 400 miles away, waiting for the water to rise and preparing for a fierce battle. The French can be considered to have won the race. With the help of the Abyssinian people, they opened a road across the African continent and occupied a section of the river from the source of the Nile to Egypt. Britain had suffered a setback, and the most important river was cut off by others. When Marchand announced that the vast area west of the Nile was French territory, Paris held triumphant celebrations. (To be continued)

Page 6

British Prime Minister Baldwin Vigorously Defends Foreign Policy; Strives to Promote Reconciliation in the Italian-Abyssinian Affair; Treaties Can Be Amended but Unilateral Cancellation is Intolerable

(London) In the British House of Commons today, following the reading of the King's Speech, a debate on the response took place. Prime Minister Baldwin vigorously defended the government's foreign policy, stating that he did not want to miss any opportunity for Britain to secure peace instead of war. The League of Nations is currently undergoing a trial, but if it can end the Italian-Abyssinian war, all peace-loving Europeans will be grateful, provided that the terms of peace are those it has stipulated.

The proposer of the motion for the response was Conservative Member of Parliament Wakefield, known as a football player, so many speakers used sporting terms in jest. The seconder was Sir Barrie, who praised Wakefield's excellent ball-handling. Labour leader Attlee said that since Mr. Chamberlain joined the government team, he has been getting the ball and kicking it. He also said that it was strange that the King's Speech used the same wording to refer to both aggressor nations and nations fulfilling their treaty obligations. The government should report in detail on the progress of all matters in the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. He did not know how a solution acceptable to Italy, Abyssinia, and the League of Nations could be achieved. Upon close examination of the King's Speech, its true focus is on increasing armaments, with everything else being merely window dressing.

Baldwin replied that he wished Parliament to discuss the very important international situation in detail, but Foreign Secretary Hoare was ill at home and may be able to attend the House of Commons tomorrow or the day after, at which time discussions could be held. Therefore, he did not wish to say much today. Any politician in this country who does not hold honorable events with other countries in the League of Nations, causing this country to fall into war, will be condemned by all. The dignity of treaties should indeed be upheld, but it is not the case that once a treaty is established, it can never be amended. Amending a treaty is one thing, while canceling a treaty is another. Unilateral cancellation is called violence, not consensual amendment. Europe is now determined to prevent the tearing up of treaties, and this year's events have proven this point, as all European countries, even though one friendly nation has now been declared an aggressor, have resolutely disregarded friendship and agreed to participate in economic sanctions that have been implemented and are considering future sanction measures. Some people believe that Britain is being too forward. It should be known that Britain has to follow other countries in fulfilling its duty. Powerful countries like Britain have to take responsibility and express their opinions at the right time. Britain will study with other countries whether there are honorable ways to end this war on terms acceptable to Abyssinia and the League of Nations.

Prime Minister Baldwin then spoke about domestic affairs, saying that the government's industrial policy over the past four years has been fundamentally about creating a state of trust among the people, protecting it with appropriate tax rates that can promote industrial prosperity. Regarding the coal mining issue, he hopes that the current discussions can not only establish understanding but also promote progress in reform. The government, in accordance with the policy stipulated in the 1930 Coal Mines Act of the previous Labour government, has decided to submit a bill immediately, agreeing to coal mine rents, as a necessary prerequisite for future work, and as part of a policy to assist the coal industry. Regarding national defense, he hopes that the House of Commons can debate this extremely important and difficult matter after the Christmas recess. The government also hopes to pass a bill to expand unemployment insurance during this parliamentary term, so that agricultural workers can benefit from this bill in the coming winter. (3rd Reuters)

Northern and Southern Fronts: Abyssinian Forces Switch to Offensive; Skirmishes Near Magaal; Southern Route Forms "Hindenburg Line"

(London) According to sources from Asmara, a large number of Abyssinian troops, well-equipped with armaments, are now advancing towards Magaal, their aim apparently being to attack Italian forces. It is reported that these troops are from the command of General Gasa, commander-in-chief of the Abyssinian forces in the north, assisted by the regular army of General Mulugheta. It is reported that the Abyssinian forces plan to strike at the southernmost point about fifteen miles south of Magaal. According to Italian bulletins, the Abyssinian advance has boosted the morale of Italian troops. If the Abyssinian forces are indeed determined to engage in a concentrated battle with Italian forces, the Italian command will have an opportunity to achieve a great victory, which will certainly be more fruitful than numerous guerrilla engagements. (4th Reuters)

A dispatch from the Abyssinian capital, Harar, reports that the "Hindenburg Line" constructed by Abyssinian forces between Daga Bur and British Somaliland, and between Harar and Jijiga, has now been completed. This project was supervised by Turkish advisor General Vehip Bey. The Abyssinian forces originally planned to hold this line to defend against a major Italian offensive that was expected to be launched shortly after the outbreak of war. However, the troops under General Nasibu, commander-in-chief of the Abyssinian forces in the south, are impatient to wait for the Italian attack. Many officers under his command are now advocating taking the offensive along the Daga Bur line, with the troops under General Lesta on the southwestern front providing support. However, several senior officers do not support this strategy, believing that Abyssinia's terrain favors defense over offense, especially because Italian weapons are sophisticated, so it is not advisable to engage in a large-scale direct confrontation with them. (4th Reuters)

Asmara: According to a communique released here today, Italian forces and the troops of Abyssinian General Seyoum have made contact twice in the past two days. In the second encounter, Italian forces again emerged victorious. Italian forces began to enter the Tembien Plateau three weeks ago, and have now engaged in their fourth skirmish near the Abaro Pass. One column of Italian forces defeated 200 Abyssinian soldiers, killing several. Italian forces suffered one white officer and five soldiers wounded. The fighting in the Tembien region has been limited to small-scale battles, but has been quite intense. So far, there has been no large-scale battle. Italian forces claim to have repeatedly emerged victorious, suffering fewer casualties than the enemy. The Abyssinian forces were scheduled to attack yesterday, as it was the feast day of Saint George, an ancient Abyssinian warrior. At the same time, one battalion of Eritrean troops in the Italian forces has advanced and reached the town of Melfa, ten miles from Gherza Moro, now within the borders of Abbi Addi, the capital of Tembien province. A small detachment of Abyssinian soldiers attacked an Italian outpost between Dolo and Magaal, but were driven back by Italian soldiers. One Italian soldier was wounded. Italian forces claim to have captured half of the Tembien region. Abyssinian General Seyoum is still leading approximately 1,000 soldiers to hold the remaining territory. (4th Reuters)

A Photo of Battlefield Misery

(London) Reuters special correspondent Collins cabled from somewhere south of Jijiga as follows: I have just witnessed the most tragic scene I have ever seen in my life. Abyssinian soldiers wounded on the battlefield have been sent to hospitals in Daga Bur and Jijiga, all suffering from severe injuries, many of whom have not received treatment for a week or more. There are no hospitals or temporary treatment stations south of Daga Bur, and the means of transporting the wounded from the front lines back behind the lines are also insufficient. Doctors and the wounded alike describe the horrors of the battlefield, saying that wounded soldiers often lie on the battlefield for days, sometimes dying from exposure, sometimes dying from festering wounds. There is a great lack of hemostatic equipment, personnel to transport the wounded, and workers skilled in first aid. However, one very special characteristic is admirable, that is, the wounded have no complaints. I spoke with a wounded non-commissioned officer who had a bullet lodged two inches deep in his lower leg. It was only today, after twelve days, that he received his first treatment. Doctors may be able to save his life, but his leg must be amputated. If not treated quickly, there is a risk of poisoning. However, two things are particularly pleasing: one is that there are relatively few wounded, with fewer than 200 in the hospitals in Jijiga and Daga Bur combined; the other is the excellent work of the Egyptian Prince Taufiq's ambulance service, which includes many British and American doctors working together with some Abyssinian doctors. (4th Reuters)

New Yu Section of the Beining Railway: The Establishment of a Puppet Supervisory Office, Appropriation of Passenger and Freight Charges, and Illegal Infringement on Railway Rights

A Tianjin dispatch reports that Yin Tong returned to Tianjin from Beijing on the morning of the 2nd. Although he accompanied Chen Yi, he also bears certain missions regarding the current North China diplomacy. Furthermore, the urgent need to address the important affairs of the Beining Railway itself is also the main reason for his hasty return north. In the afternoon of the 2nd, the Railway Bureau held an important bureau affairs meeting, attended by staff above the section chief level. Although this reporter was unable to attend in person due to other commitments, the points to be discussed had already been instructed to Deputy Bureau Chiefs Lu Mengxiong and Zheng Shi Zhao. The core of the important discussions at the meeting revolved around the illegal infringement on railway rights by the establishment of a supervisory office for the Xin Yu section of the Beining Railway by the puppet Jidong Anti-Communist Autonomous Committee, and a contingency plan was formulated. The section from Xinhe to Yu Guan on the Beining Railway is over 270 kilometers long, accounting for about two-thirds of the entire length of the current Beining Railway mainline. It has always been the main source of revenue for railway freight and passenger transport. Recently, the Railway Bureau's revenue, coinciding with the peak season, has averaged about 2.4 to 2.5 million per month, with the Xin Yu section accounting for over 1.3 million. All railway materials and rolling stock, except for those in Tianjin and Ping, are mostly located in this section. Important facilities such as the Xinhe Station material factory, Tangshan rolling stock factory, and the Chegong branches in Luoxian and Shanhaiguan are all crucial construction sites for the entire railway. If the puppet organization implements its supervision and directly severs this section, it would be fatal to the Beining Railway. However, until recently, although the puppet organization had established a railway supervisory office, it had not actually infringed on railway administration. Only the daily income from freight and passenger transport at Tangshan Station was being appropriated, but the amount was still small. Some materials and furniture stored at the Tangshan rolling stock factory were also being requisitioned. The local rolling stock section chief and stationmaster were powerless to resist and could only allow them to take what they wanted. The Luoxian Iron Bridge, Xinhe, Tangshan, and other rolling stock and material factories were being monitored by personnel dispatched by Zhao Lei's 4th Security Brigade. Apart from this, the order at other stations remained normal. According to the Beining Railway Bureau's speculation, the reason why the puppet organization has not taken over the stations is because it is concerned about the British capital invested in the railway and because the division of the Xin Yu section from the Beining mainline would inevitably lead to a sharp decline in revenue, at most only 700,000 per month. And even from that amount, the freight charges for coal transport recorded in Kai Luan, about 300,000 per month, would have to be deducted. The remaining amount would not be sufficient to cover expenses, so they could not help but be hesitant and wavering. The puppet supervisory office head, Lu Qiu, originally served as the secretary of the Beining Railway Bureau. His real name is Zhen Huan. In July, he was hired by Yin Rugeng to serve as the chief of the General Affairs Section of the Luan Yu District Administrative Commissioner's Office. Now, seeing that he has turned traitor, his puppet supervisory office is located in Tangshan and is divided into six sections. The personnel for each section have already been announced: Bo Zhu is the chief of the General Affairs Section, Han Zikui is the chief of the Accounting Section, Chen Juesheng (current chief of the Tangshan rolling stock section of the Beining Railway) is the chief of the Rolling Stock Section, Xie Zhen (current director of the Tangshan Iron Factory of the Beining Railway) is the chief of the Machinery Section, Xu Kaixian (Tangshan Station engineer) is the chief of the Works Section, and Qu Shihe is the chief of the Police Section. Although some current Beining Railway employees have been appointed by the puppet organization, they have not accepted the appointments and are not subject to their control. Lu Qiu secretly came to Tianjin a few days ago and had secret contacts with the Tianjin office of the South Manchuria Railway. Over the past three days, dozens of senior employees of the South Manchuria Railway have come to Tianjin together, supposedly to accept the appointment of the puppet organization, under the guise of entrusted management, to take over the railway affairs of the Xin Yu section. The Beining Railway is paying close attention to this matter and has formulated preventive measures. (3rd)

Central Government Loan to Aid Jiangxi Province's Finances

The Economic Commission Will Also Provide Loans to Aid Rural Areas

A Nanchang dispatch reports that due to economic depression and market recession in Jiangxi Province, the Chamber of Commerce, the Money Trade Association, and the Remittance Exchange Association have successively appealed to the central government to allocate legal tender to save the dying industry and commerce and avoid an unmanageable collapse. According to financial circles, the matter of the province borrowing funds from the central government has been successfully resolved through the efforts of Chairman Xiong and Finance Director Wu, who have repeatedly contacted Minister Kong and the Central, China, and Communications Banks in Beijing and Shanghai. The Bank of China will allocate 1 million yuan in legal tender to the Remittance Exchange Association as a fund for discounting acceptance bills, 1.4 million yuan will be handed over to the provincial Yumin Bank for lending to various industries, and another 2 million yuan will be handed over to the Central, China, and Communications Banks for exchange into legal tender. With these 3.4 million yuan, the market in the province should be able to become somewhat active. As for the year-end settlement period, the funds will be lent by the banks to the money shops, and then by the money shops to various industries, to cope with year-end expenses and resources for the opening of the market next year. Furthermore, the National Economic Commission previously planned to establish cooperative banks in four provinces, setting up branches in Jiangxi, Hubei, Anhui, and Hunan to lend to rural cooperatives in those areas, which in turn would lend to farmers to aid rural areas, with a capital of 10 million yuan. Recently, the Economic Commission decided that setting up separate banks would involve excessive expenses, and the loan to cooperative societies to aid rural area item will be entrusted to the Central, China, and Communications Banks. (November 30)

The local Public Security Bureau has repeatedly issued orders strictly prohibiting women from electrically curling their hair. However, the barbershops, driven by profit, secretly set up rooms and continued to curl hair as usual. After Director Chen learned of this, he ordered the various sub-bureaus under his jurisdiction to confiscate all hair curling irons in the area. After receiving the order, Hong Houchang, the director of the First Sub-bureau, specifically ordered two senior policemen on the 4th to confiscate the hair curling irons from four establishments: Wanguo, Meirongxuan, Heyuanli, and Shijie at the Xinsheng Road intersection, all located at Chong'an Temple. The various sub-bureaus also dispatched police to rigorously enforce the order at six other establishments on the roads: Yixin, Dahua, Meili, Meihua, Shixin in Badou Alley, and Wuxi in Beicheng.

Luhe: Over 6,000 Yuan Stolen from a Money Shop

Yifenghou Money Shop was established by Wang Zhan in this county as a sole proprietorship. It has been in business for a hundred years and its operations have been quite successful. On the evening of the 28th, it was discovered that a large sum of money had been stolen. At the time of the count, it was found that 6,040 yuan was missing. The next morning, upon learning of the incident, the owner immediately reported it to the county government's detective team for investigation and prosecution, as a basis for verification and handling.

International Commercial Telegram

Reuter's Special Commercial Telegram, December 4

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today was 140 shillings 11.5 pence, down 1.5 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market was stable today. Spot and futures prices both fell 0.0625. There were more purchases from the United States and more sales from India.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was very quiet this morning. The opening exchange rate for British pounds to US dollars was $4.934375, higher by 0.0625 than the closing rate of the US Central Bank yesterday. At 1:00 PM, it fell by 125 to $4.933125, and there were no further changes.

British-French: The opening rate was 74 francs 90, up 9 pounds. At 11:00 AM, it fell by 2 pounds, and at noon, it rose by 3 pounds. At 1:00 PM, the price returned to 74 francs 88.

Cotton and Wheat

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened down 125. It continued to fall 25 due to profit-taking by bulls. The opening price for coarse grains was firm, but later trended lower.

American Cotton: The New York cotton market saw prices shrink by 10 points at the opening due to large-scale sales by the US Cotton Public Storage Organization. Subsequently, the price continued to fall by 5 points due to profit-taking by bulls. It is expected that the Agricultural Adjustment Administration will be ruled unconstitutional by the Supreme Court. Merchants are very pessimistic about this. Cotton exports are said to be still good.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market rose 75 at 1:00 PM today to 6 shillings 025.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market fell slightly today. At 1:00 PM, the price was 6.48, down 2 pence.

Rubber

New York: The opening price of rubber in New York rose by 17 points. The impact of the increase in the quota for rubber from the Dutch East Indies, which is beneficial to the shorts, has now been reduced. Subsequently, the price continued to rise due to purchases, but then fell slightly due to profit-taking by bulls.

London: The rubber market was stable this morning. The trading price for April-May futures was 6.375 pence, higher by 0.0625 than yesterday's closing price.

Securities

New York: The securities market opened with mixed gains and losses this morning. Prices rose later due to good demand. Public utility stocks also rose initially, but then fell due to profit-taking. The Dow Jones 30 industrial average opened at 143.99, up 41 points.

Local News

Jianghai Customs Issues a Proclamation on the Measures for Sanctions Against Italy: Violators Will Be Treated as Smugglers, Handled According to Customs Regulations

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Balunsen, Commissioner of Customs, issued Proclamation No. 1478 yesterday, stating that the Ministry of Finance has ordered that with regards to the third and fourth recommendations of the League of Nations on the sanctions against Italy, the Executive Yuan has ordered that the following implementation measures be taken: (1) The following goods, when shipped to Italy and its territories, are prohibited from December 1st: (A) Horses, mules, donkeys, camels, and all kinds of transport animals; (B) Rubber; (C) Bauxite, aluminum, aluminum oxide, iron ore and scrap iron, ore, magnesium, nickel, titanium, tungsten, and their ores, and alloys of iron such as "copper steel," "high-speed steel," "manganese silicon steel," "manganese silicon aluminum steel," tin, and their ores. The above includes all unrefined minerals and metals, ores, scraps, and alloys; (2) From December 1st, no further commercial contracts may be entered into with any Italian organization, company, or individual regarding the import of Italian goods into China; (3) Purchase contracts for which payment has not been made before December 1st should be cancelled immediately; (4) Purchase contracts for which payment has been made in full or 20% or more before December 1st are exempt from cancellation; (5) Italian goods imported into China that are already en route are exempt from import prohibition, but only if they enter the country before January 1, 1936. After this date, import is prohibited; (6) Goods produced in Italy but processed in other countries, as well as goods manufactured partly in Italy or its territories and partly in other countries, if imported after January 1, 1936, shall also be prohibited from import, unless 25% or more of the value of the goods is derived from some form of processing that occurs after the goods leave Italy or its territories; (7) The following items are not prohibited from import even if they enter the country after January 1, 1936: (A) Gold and silver bullion and coins; (B) Books, newspapers, magazines, and maps; (C) Nautical charts, printed matter, printing plates, and music; (D) Items carried by passengers; (8) All goods that violate the prohibition, whether imported or exported, shall be treated as smuggled goods and handled according to the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations. This proclamation is hereby issued for the information of all merchants, to be strictly observed. December 3, 1935, Republic of China.

Reorganization of the Central Bank into a Reserve Bank: Decision to Recruit Commercial Shares

By Law, It Cannot Exceed 40%

The Board Meeting This Month is Being Prepared and a Decision Can Be Made

Xin Sheng She reports that since the Ministry of Finance implemented the new currency system policy, it has decided to reorganize the Central Bank into a Central Reserve Bank. Regarding preparatory matters, a meeting of the Board of Directors was held on the 25th of last month. Executive Directors Kong Xiangxi, Chen Xing, Ye Yu, Xu Kan, Zhang Jia'ao, and Tang Dumin, and Directors Qian Xinzhi and Chen Guangfu, among others, were present. A general decision has already been made. As for the recruitment of commercial shares, it is said that after the Board Meeting this month has passed it, it can be carried out. According to Article 7 of the Central Bank Organization Law, "When necessary, the Central Bank may, with the resolution of the Board of Directors and the approval of the Board of Supervisors, apply to the National Government for approval to expand the total capital amount, and may recruit commercial shares, but the total number of commercial shares shall not exceed 40% of the total capital amount. When recruiting commercial shares, domestic financial institutions engaged in banking and money lending shall have priority to subscribe. Only when the commercial shares purchased by various legal entities have reached 30% or more of the total capital amount of the Central Bank may individuals invest, but individual investment shall be subject to the approval of the Minister of Finance." It is found that the bank's capital is 100 million yuan in national currency. This time, the recruitment of commercial shares cannot exceed 40 million yuan in national currency at most.

Qianzhuang [Money Shops] Have Already Claimed Legal Tender

The Overseas Exchange Banks Association Contributes Opinions to Finance Minister Kong

Xin Sheng She reports that after the Ministry of Finance stipulated that banks and qianzhuang should use 60% cash and 40% reserves to claim legal tender from the Central, China, and Communications Banks, the member banks of the Banking Association and the member qianzhuang of the Qianye Association have all complied. The executive committee of the Qianye Association also resolved to provide 40% reserves themselves. If treasury bonds and public debt bonds are sent to the Qianye United Reserve, they will be collected by the Reserve and an additional 40% reserve will be added to the total amount of silver coins previously handed over to the Central, China, and Communications Banks. Legal tender was claimed from the three banks the previous day and distributed to member qianzhuang for use.

The nine member banks of the Shanghai Overseas Exchange Banks Association, including Chartered Bank, HSBC, Yokohama Specie Bank, Banque de l'Indochine, Citibank, Banque Belge pour l'Étranger, Nederlandsche Handel-Maatschappij, Banco Italo-Cinese, Deutsch-Asiatische Bank, as well as the eleven member banks including Banque Franco-Chinoise, Bank of Taiwan, Sumitomo Bank, Mitsui Bank, Bank of Chosen, Mitsubishi Bank, Chase Bank, Andersen, American Express Great Britain, and Sino-French Industrial Bank, after being ordered to hand over their cash reserves and exchange them for legal tender from the Central Bank, have held several meetings to discuss the matter. They have accepted the principle and the chairman, Mr. Kirk Ming of Chartered Bank, has met with Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi to contribute his opinions. Mr. Hu Mingchun Returned to Shanghai Yesterday from Tibet

Mr. Hu Mingchun, a native of Zhejiang, went to study at the International University in India in 1933 with his own funds. Recognizing that the government was actively handling Mongolian and Tibetan border affairs, he went to Tibet to specialize in studying Tibetan and took the opportunity to investigate the situation in Tibet, so as to be of service to the government. Since entering Tibet, it has been two years. Mr. Hu felt that he had mastered Tibetan, so he took a ship Conte Verde of Italian lines, returning home via India, arriving in Shanghai yesterday. The reporter of Guowen News Agency met with Mr. Hu yesterday. According to him, the details of his entry into Tibet and the attitude of Tibetans towards Chinese people are as follows:

Entry into Tibet

Mr. Hu originally studied at Tagore's International University in India, where he met Tibetan students and got along very well with them. He studied Tibetan and Tibetan writing. When Huang Musong and others were sent to Tibet, he accompanied them as a staff member. While in Tibet, he received guidance from the famous monk Tu Tian Sang Pei and gained a good understanding of Buddhist scriptures.

Tibetan Thinking

Tibetan thinking is still consistent with traditional thinking. They have a deep understanding and faith in the head of state. They respect the Chinese people very much. In ordinary conversations, they generally regard the Chinese as being one level higher than Tibetans. Since Special Envoy Huang entered Tibet, the Tibetan people's view of the Chinese people has been better, and their faith has also been very strong.

Departure from Tibet

When Mr. Hu left Tibet this time, he encountered the British political officer in Sikkim, Williamson, and others heading towards Tibet when he passed through Kalimpang on the border between India and Tibet. It is said that their entry into Tibet this time was to undertake some mission regarding the development of Indo-Tibetan transportation.

Three Bureaus Discuss Establishing Railway Postal and Telegraph Stations

It Has Been Decided to Implement This First at the Nine Major Stations of Jinghu, Huhang, and Ningbo. The Establishment of Other Stations Will Be Discussed by the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways.

Dagong News Agency reports that after discussions between the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways, three measures have been decided upon regarding the establishment of postal and telegraph agencies along railway stations: (1) The establishment of postal and telegraph agencies at railway stations by the Ministry of Railways will be trialled first on the Jinghu and Huhangyong lines, based on the three conditions proposed by the Ministry of Railways; (2) The temporary measures for the establishment of railway station postal and telegraph agencies originally stipulated by the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Bureaus, the Shanghai Postal Bureau, and the Telegraph Bureau are considered to be in line with the three conditions proposed by the Ministry of Railways and may be approved for trial implementation; (3) The Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways will separately instruct the two Railway Bureaus and the two bureaus in Shanghai, the Postal Bureau and Telegraph Bureau, to consult and set a date for implementation, and will separately order the two Railway Administrations, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, and the Postal Administration to comply with the implementation. It has now been decided that the postal and telegraph station agencies will first be piloted on the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Bureaus, and it has been stipulated that (A) the Jinghu Line: (1) Nanjing, (2) Bojiang, (3) Changzhou, (4) Wuxi, (5) Shanghai North Station; (B) the Huhang Line: (1) Shanghai South Station, (2) Songjiang, (3) Jiaxing, (4) Hangzhou, etc., are nine major stations. In the future, if the operation is successful, they will be increased at any time. Other railway stations such as Pinghan, Jinpu, Longhai, Jiaoji, Zhengtai, and Beining will continue to be established. It is reported that the three bureaus will proceed with consultations on the joint establishment of agency measures and internal procedures as soon as the Ministry's orders arrive in Shanghai, and will decide on the implementation date after everything has been settled.

Premier Wang's Back Wound Has Not Healed Yet; It Will Recover with Rest

Central News Agency reports that there have been various rumors recently about Premier Wang's condition, some saying that it is trending towards becoming serious and others saying that he has gotten out of bed to walk and even strolled in the garden. In fact, both are overly speculative. According to reliable sources, when Dr. Wang underwent surgery on the 29th of last month, his spirits weakened and his breathing became weak due to the excessive amount of time it took. An examination of his urine that afternoon showed that the sugar content had increased eightfold compared to the morning, and acetone was found in it (the presence of acetone in the urine of ordinary people can cause dizziness). Fortunately, Dr. Noel treated him carefully and he gradually improved. However, there was still a pulse stop phenomenon on the 2nd, and he still felt stomach pain on the 3rd. These were all due to the effects of the injury and surgery, so the wound on his back has not healed yet. Not only is he unable to walk, but he is also unable to sit up. He has been confined to bed all day. Dr. Wang recently sent a telegram to Ambassador Guo Fuchu (Taiqi), saying that his injury will not lead to death or disability, and that he has emerged from danger. As for the injury and the recurrence of old illnesses, it will only recover with rest. Judging from this telegram, Wang's condition can be clearly seen, and the overly speculative rumors are not credible.

In addition, it is reported that Premier Wang has not seen guests for many days since coming to Shanghai for treatment, in accordance with the doctor's orders. On the afternoon of the previous day, he received Chen Gongbo and Gu Mengyu at his bedside. Although the conversation was very short, he felt insomnia that night. At around 11:00 AM yesterday, he received Tang Youren once. After a doctor's examination in the afternoon, it was discovered that he had inflammation and swelling of the bile ducts and also felt stomach pain. Therefore, all three doctors firmly instructed Wang not to see guests.

A Good Opportunity to Promote National Products in Southeast Asia

Central News Agency reports that trade between China and Southeast Asia is currently being actively planned and developed by the government and famous manufacturers. Since the implementation of the new currency policy, domestic finance has become stable and the exchange rate has also stabilized due to the government's efforts. Therefore, developing foreign trade is a good opportunity. Chinese exporters to Southeast Asia have always lacked a complete organization. In the past, some merchants, tempted by petty profits, mixed in inferior products and reduced quality, so their credit was not outstanding and they could not compete with foreign merchants with complete organizations. This time, Song Faxiang, our Consul-General in Batavia, has returned to China and has repeatedly discussed matters with domestic industrial, commercial, and financial circles. According to Wang Xingyao, director of the China National Products Promotion Association, international trade development must have a complete organization, such as the promotion of goods and the investigation of local market conditions, and must rely on banks to guarantee payments, so as to avoid losses due to the difficulty or delay in collecting payments. Consul-General Song has returned to China and reported that the failure of national product quality to meet standardization is an important reason for the decline in trade. Therefore, manufacturers themselves should strive for excellent and uniform quality to ensure outstanding credit. In terms of promotion, setting up sample display centers in important areas would not be too costly and would be very effective. As for the investigation of local market conditions, he has requested Song's assistance in guaranteeing the collection of payments and has contacted the Overseas Chinese Bank. If all aspects proceed smoothly, it can be realized in the shortest time. This is a major innovation in China's foreign trade, and the development of trade can be predicted.

Germany: New Initiatives in Scientific Academy Awards

The German Academy of Sciences, in commemoration of the scholar Wilhelm von Humboldt, recognizing his contributions to science and his spirit of sacrifice in linguistics, has decided to donate the "Humboldt Medal" on the centenary of Humboldt's death. This is intended to reward those from various countries who are deeply engaged in the study of the German language. This medal will be awarded by the Academy once a year. People of any nationality (but must be non-German and whose native language is not German) are eligible to apply, with particular attention given to students in foreign schools and language classes. Three winners will be selected from each country. The most outstanding candidate will not only receive the medal but will also be granted the benefit of half-price participation in a four-week research course held at the Academy in Munich, Germany. Thesis submissions for the competition should be no more than four pages long and preferably typed for the convenience of the judges. Applicants must clearly state their full name and address, and must also specify where they studied German. Applications should be sent directly to the Academy's general office in Germany, arriving no later than March 15, 1926. On April 8 of the same year, the Academy will announce the names of the winners in German and foreign newspapers. The competition topics for 1936 have already been drafted and announced by the Academy.

Chairman Chiang's Order: Register Opium Addicts Within a Deadline, Mobilize Land and Water Forces Today to Investigate Opium Addicts, Expand Propaganda to Promote Awareness Among Opium Addicts in the Concessions

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau is enforcing the compulsory registration of opium addicts. Yesterday, it received an order from Chairman Chiang to complete the registration within the year and report on the progress of the registration. The Bureau has decided to launch a full-scale land and water mobilization today to investigate opium addicts. The details are as follows, as reported by a reporter from Dagong News Agency:

Chairman Chiang's Order Sets a Deadline for Completion

Chairman Chiang recently sent a telegram to the Shanghai Municipal Government, stating that the registration of opium addicts must be completed within this year. The telegram stated: "The strict prohibition of opium, to the extent that all provinces and cities across the country completely eradicate opium poppies and opium addicts by 1940, has been repeatedly regulated and urged by this Chairman. The results have gradually improved, and the international community has praised this. This year, the Central Government has again issued a clear order, with this Chairman concurrently serving as the National Opium Suppression Commissioner, to ensure the thorough implementation of the deadline for the ban. The simultaneous intensification of banning cultivation and smoking is essential, and no delay is permitted. The registration of opium addicts in various provinces and cities is a crucial key to the strict enforcement of the ban on smoking. This has been repeatedly ordered by the Headquarters. Therefore, I reiterate this clear order: all provinces and cities must thoroughly complete this task by 1935, and all must report the registration progress and detailed numbers of opium addicts to the Headquarters for verification by the end of January 1936. No procrastination is allowed. Otherwise, the responsible officials will be held accountable. It is hoped that you will comply accordingly." After receiving the order, the Municipal Government instructed the Public Security Bureau to comply.

Land and Water Mobilization for Investigation Today

In order to completely eliminate opium and complete the registration of opium addicts, the Municipal Public Security Bureau began a second round of investigations. In recent days, more than 900 unregistered opium addicts have been detained and sent to drug rehabilitation centers. Starting today, a full-scale land and water mobilization will be implemented throughout the city for strict investigation. The Opium Addict Registration Section of the Bureau will send personnel to work with the police stations in various districts to search house by house. The Water Patrol Team, led by Captain Wu Xingbo, will assist in the water areas. It is essential to register all opium addicts within this year and persuade them to quit in stages.

Opium Addicts in the Concessions Should Register Quickly

Regarding opium addicts in the Concession areas, an agreement has been reached with the Concession authorities that opium offenders will be sent to the municipal drug rehabilitation hospital for confinement. After 20 days, they will be sent back to the court for execution. To facilitate poor opium addicts, a simplified method of voluntary registration for poor opium addicts in the Concession areas has been established. Those who have registered have been enthusiastic, but due to the vastness of the area, many are still waiting to see what happens. The Bureau emphasizes that this compulsory registration period will not be extended after it expires. If unregistered opium addicts are found in the future, their travel will be restricted, and the Concession authorities will resolutely assist in strict prohibition. There will be no more opportunities to escape the law. Therefore, it is hoped that opium addicts in the Concession areas will quickly register with the Municipal Public Security Bureau. A liaison office in the Chinese area is sufficient for acceptance. To ensure that opium addicts in the Concession areas deeply understand the importance of opium prohibition, the Bureau has specially arranged for the screening of opium prohibition films in various cinemas and entertainment venues before the main feature. It has also scheduled Bureau Chief Cai Jingjun and Chief Inspector Wang Dasui to take turns broadcasting propaganda on various radio stations within days, hoping that opium addicts residing in the Concession areas will quickly realize the situation.

The army usually conducts them in the interior of Luzon, while the navy conducts them along the coast. All available warships will participate. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Instructions: Stamping Required for Renewed Extended Contracts

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday replied to the Zhonghan Glass Factory, instructing that stamping is required for renewed extended contracts. The letter stated: "Regarding your letter asking whether stamp duty should be affixed to mortgage loan extensions, according to Article 9 of the Stamp Duty Law, if a document with already affixed stamp duty is modified due to a change in circumstances and continues to be used, the changed portion should still be supplemented with stamp duty. In this case, your factory and the original mortgagor have agreed to a one-year extension due to the expiration of the original one-year term and the inability to redeem the mortgage. Although it is stated that the previous contract remains valid, the term of the original contract has changed. In fact, a new contract has been established, and the previous contract has lost its validity. The previous stamping of the contract is no longer valid and should be stamped according to Item 19 of the Stamp Duty Law Tax Rate Table.

Guoyang Representatives Beg for Relief from Drought Disaster

The Renji Road Chinese and Foreign Relief Society has been actively working on disaster areas along the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers, and winter relief will continue to be provided to Tianmen in Hubei. However, northern Anhui is uniquely suffering from continuous drought. Ying Shang, Fuyang, Linquan, Taihe, Fengtai, and Mengcheng counties have all reported severe drought and no harvest. Relief is urgently needed. This has been reported in previous news. The Society has now received Mr. Wang Cibin, a representative from Guoyang, who has personally come to Shanghai to beg for assistance, his report is recorded below: "Guoyang has suffered from years of famine, and resources are exhausted. This year is even worse. Since the beginning of summer, the drought demon has ravaged the land, and the autumn crops have been burned to ashes. The entire county of 187,000 acres has no harvest. Even if wheat is replanted, it will take six months. As winter approaches, the famine victims will suffer even more from hunger and cold. Currently, approximately 330,000 people are awaiting relief. We earnestly request that assistance be allocated before the New Year to provide emergency relief, and that work relief be provided in the spring. Your examination and implementation of assistance are requested." Northern Anhui has always been known for its poverty, and now it is suffering from both drought and floods. Winter is also approaching. How can the people survive? It is a pity that people are focusing on the floods and are unaware of the severity of the drought. The greatest virtue is saving lives. It is urgently hoped that all sectors will hear the news and quickly provide assistance.
