Ministry of Communications and Ministry of Railways Agreed: Both Railways Will Act as Agents for Postal and Telegraph Services

Measures for Cooperation between the Two Railways and the Shanghai Telegraph and Postal Services; Postal and Telegraph Agencies to be Established at Each Station to Benefit Passengers

The Guomin News Agency reports that the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways, in order to facilitate railway passengers sending telegrams and mailing letters at any time, have specifically planned to establish postal and telegraph agencies at each station. Regarding the issue of sending and receiving telegrams, the Railway Administration has discussed the procedures with the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, and they have been officially implemented. Stations such as the Shanghai North Station and the major stations along the two railways have been gradually established. It is now known that the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways have consulted and decided to approve the trial operation. The postal services will be handled jointly by the two railway bureaus and the Shanghai Postal Bureau. Three measures have been decided: (1) Railway stations will establish postal and telegraph agencies. Based on the three conditions proposed by the Ministry of Railways, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways will be the first to trial the operation. (2) The original agreement between the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus and the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau and Postal Bureau to establish railway station postal agencies is consistent with the items proposed by the Ministry of Railways and may be approved for trial operation. (3) The Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways will separately instruct the two railway bureaus and the Shanghai Postal and Telegraph Bureaus to consult.

Reorganization of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau: Operating Automobiles at the Xiaguan Station in Beijing; Passengers Will Be Picked Up and Dropped Off by the Public Automobile Company

The Xiaguan Station of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway is an important transportation hub for passengers. In the past, dozens of cars picked up and dropped off passengers at the station. These cars were operated by various automobile companies in Beijing that were licensed by the Railway Bureau. However, due to the dilapidated equipment and inconsistent management of these companies, the Railway Bureau decided to improve the situation. Last summer, the Nanjing Communications Automobile Company collected various unlicensed "chicken cars" and obtained more than 20 licenses to operate at the Xiaguan Station. After more than a year, the results were not satisfactory. It is said that they also failed to obtain a license from the Ministry of Industry. After investigation, the Bureau terminated their licensed operation at the end of November this year and selected the Beijing Public Automobile Company to send cars to the station to pick up and drop off passengers in accordance with regulations starting on December 1. However, when the public automobiles arrived at the station, the Communications Automobile Company suddenly sent cars to enter the station area and surround the public automobiles, preventing them from operating. At that time, a passenger train arrived, and the railway police on duty, in order to maintain passenger traffic, advised the Communications Automobile Company. The company ignored the advice and sent more cars to rush into the station, injuring a railway policeman. The Bureau detained three drivers involved in the incident and used force to suppress the situation, and the drama was finally settled. Currently, the pick-up and drop-off of passengers at the Xiaguan Station is handled by the Public Automobile Company. It is reported that the company's vehicles are better equipped, and passengers are very satisfied.

Shanghai Municipal Branch of the National Medical Association: Telegram Urges Prompt Promulgation of the Chinese Medicine Regulations; Issue of Equal Treatment for Chinese and Western Medicine

After the directors of the Shanghai Municipal Branch of the National Medical Association took office, they actively carried out various tasks. Recently, they sent a telegram to the First Plenary Session of the Kuomintang, stating: "The opening of your meeting is a pivotal event for the central authorities. Your contributions to national construction are admired by all. We are fortunate to read in the newspapers the review report of the proposals of the Fifth Plenary Session, in which the first proposal, 'The government should treat Chinese and Western medicine equally to promote academics and benefit the people,' and the review opinion, 'Whether the Chinese Medicine Regulations should be properly revised is to be discussed and considered by the Central Executive Committee as soon as possible,' are highly appreciated. Medical treatment concerns the lives of the people, regardless of wealth or poverty. It is considered essential and should be based on practical use. There should be no boundaries. In recent years, misunderstandings have led to disputes. There are no established rules for management, and opinions are often biased. Improvements are slow. The chairman and members are compassionate and fair. We hope that the regulations will be promulgated soon so that there is something to follow. We are extremely grateful. Xia Yingtang, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Branch of the Central National Medical Association, and Deputy Directors Ding Zhongying and Gu Weichuan."

The Shanghai Medical Circle Chunqiu Society telegraphed the First Plenary Session of the Kuomintang a few days ago, stating, "To the Honorable Members of the First Plenary Session in Nanjing, medicine is an academic discipline that protects the health of the nation and has no national boundaries. Chinese medicine has been passed down for thousands of years, and scholars from the East and West have paid close attention to it. However, due to the lack of adequate protection and promotion by the government, it has not been fully developed. The Fifth Plenary Session passed a proposal for 'The government to treat Chinese and Western medicine equally to promote academics and benefit the people.' The Chinese Medicine Regulations were drafted by the Legislative Yuan in December 1933, but the Executive Yuan has not yet promulgated them. Whether this policy is implemented or not has a significant impact on academics and people's livelihood. We request that this matter be promulgated as soon as possible to appease the people. We anxiously await your reply. Zhang Zanchen, Chairman of the Shanghai Medical Circle Chunqiu Society."

Charitable Organizations Petition the Municipal Government: Increase Subsidies for the Shelter for the Poor and Report on the Progress of the Collective Discussions

The Federation of Charitable Organizations in Shanghai petitioned the Municipal Government yesterday for funds to operate the Shelter for the Poor. The original text stated, "Regarding the report on the preparations for operating the Shelter for the Poor and requesting an increase in funding, the reason is: The market in Shanghai has declined this year, rural areas are bankrupt, industry and commerce are depressed, and the number of unemployed civilians has increased. In addition, after the floods in various provinces, disaster victims have come to Shanghai in droves, lacking food and clothing and urgently needing relief. The Civilian Shelter for the Poor, which has been established by this Association for many years, should be operated according to the previous case. The Social Affairs Bureau has also sent a letter requesting early preparations. A meeting of various charitable organizations was convened on the 21st of this month to discuss the matter. It was decided to follow the method of the previous year and borrow the Chaozhou Guild Hall on South Railway Station Road as the first shelter and the Chaohui Mountain Villa on Xietu Road as the second shelter. After the two shelters are full, they will be expanded. However, the Chaohui Mountain Villa is currently occupied by a security team. This Association will find a house on behalf of the team and negotiate their relocation. At the same time, the Social Affairs Bureau will be requested to send personnel to contact the team to facilitate the process. Because the Chaohui Mountain Villa has larger houses, it can accommodate more than 3,000 people. At this time of financial difficulty, it is more economical to concentrate the shelters in one place. Therefore, it is necessary to relocate the security team. The start of admission is expected to be around December 10. If the weather turns cold suddenly, it will be advanced at any time. Currently, the necessary preparations are being made in advance. Regarding the admission expenses, the various charitable organizations pledged to donate approximately 11,000 yuan at the meeting on the 21st. However, according to previous expenses, at least 20,000 yuan is needed. This year, the number of admissions is expected to increase, and the expenses will also increase. The amount pledged by the charitable organizations is far from sufficient, and fundraising is extremely difficult. The Municipal Government allocates 1,000 yuan annually. We earnestly request that the difficult situation this year be considered, which is even more difficult than in previous years. In addition to the allocation according to the previous case, an additional 2,000 yuan is requested. This Association will strive to raise the remaining funds to cope with the situation. In addition to submitting another report when admissions begin on a regular basis, this document is prepared and submitted to you. We hope that you will review and order compliance. Thank you."

Fake Company: Master Swindler Ma Tianji Captured

Ma Tianji, who specializes in setting up fake companies to defraud goods, was captured after defrauding a large quantity of furs from various fur shops in the International Settlement, worth over 30,000 yuan, and fleeing. The victims reported the case to the Lao Zha Police Station. It is reported that yesterday, detectives in Ximen Zhaojiabang Road, in collaboration with police officers, arrested Ma Tianji, a 27-year-old native of Shaoxing. After being taken to the police station for questioning, he confessed to defrauding the furs for pawning and using the money. Several accomplices are also involved. The police are currently investigating the fugitives and retrieving the stolen goods from various pawnshops for submission to the court for trial.

Girl Injured by Car

Liu Jiangshi, a woman from Changzhou residing at 57 Hengmao Lane, West End of the Ba Xian Qiao in the French Concession, instructed her thirteen-year-old daughter, Lan Ying, to deliver a postal card to the post office across the street yesterday (the 4th) at 2:50 PM. Local: Snow Pellets Began to Fall Yesterday, Bitter Wind, Freezing Cold, Snow Stopped by Evening with Intermittent Rain

The local weather, since the beginning of winter, had been extremely warm. The south wind blew gently, as warm as spring. The flowers, grass, trees, and plants in the suburbs showed no signs of withering. The growth of crops and vegetables in the fields was relatively easy. However, insects thrived. Normally, by this deep winter period, even if they were not frozen to death, they would have already hibernated. Now, they remained active, causing significant damage to the fields. Until the end of last week, it gradually turned cold. Yesterday morning, dark clouds gathered, and the sunlight disappeared. The north wind was bitter, and the cold was biting. At around 12 noon, snow pellets suddenly fell, making a pattering sound on the roofs. Later, the snow was mixed with light rain, which continued intermittently until evening. This first snow in the suburbs of Shanghai should be enough to kill pests and benefit farmers.

Youth Propaganda Group Held Anti-Drug Rally Yesterday; Representatives Spoke on the Significance of Opium Suppression

The Shanghai Youth Propaganda Group held a meeting last night at 7:30 PM in the group's auditorium. Over a thousand people participated. Group Chairman Yin Yong presided over the meeting and reported on the significance of the event, stating that the purpose of the meeting was to assist the government in promoting opium suppression efforts and hoped that the public would voluntarily quit smoking, so as not to betray the original intention of convening this meeting. He then gave a detailed report on the source of opium imports and the significance of opium suppression. Next, Ye Shu, a representative of the Public Security Bureau, spoke in detail about the purpose of the local authorities' determination to suppress opium and the strict regulations for punishing opium offenders. He urged local smokers to quickly and voluntarily quit smoking in order to achieve the goal of strengthening the body and the country. Subsequently, representatives from the Municipal Party Committee, Ji Hao, and the Health Bureau, Shen Qifeng, spoke in succession (speeches omitted). After the representatives finished speaking, the meeting distributed various propaganda materials related to opium suppression in the city to each of the more than one thousand participants, and explained any unclear points. Finally, a five-act vernacular drama "Quit or Not Quit" was performed. The plot focused on the various situations and harms of smokers before and after quitting, with profound implications and excellent performances. The meeting adjourned at around 10:00 PM.

Flat-Bed Cart Mutual Aid Society Expresses Opinions on Wheel Modifications

Requests that the Weight Limit for Vehicles Remain as Previously Agreed and Writes to Police Station to Not Detain Carts Without Reason

The Public Concession Municipal Council previously deemed that flat-bed carts and rickshaws hindered traffic and damaged road surfaces and planned to increase vehicle taxes to restrict and ban them. This decision was cancelled only after strenuous negotiations by the local Flat-Bed Cart Industry Mutual Aid Society. Recently, the Municipal Council suddenly issued an order limiting cart owners to modifying their wheels to protect road surfaces. However, the Flat-Bed Cart Industry Mutual Aid Society found the specified design inconvenient for work and increased the burden. Therefore, it notified its members, collected opinions, and decided at a meeting to write to the Municipal Council expressing its opinions and to write to the Lao Zha Police Station to negotiate the issue of the unwarranted expulsion of rickshaws. The original letters are recorded below.

Expressing Opinions on Wheel Modifications

The Shanghai Flat-Bed Cart Industry Mutual Aid Society writes to the Municipal Council expressing its opinions on wheel modifications, stating: "We have recently learned that your esteemed authorities have stipulated that, from July 1st of next year, the wheels of flat-bed carts and rickshaws must be modified to three and a half-inch wide angled iron wheels or two-inch solid rubber tires. Our members are deeply concerned about this. They all say that if three and a half-inch angled iron wheels are installed, they will be clumsy and heavy, making business extremely difficult. Installing rubber tires would also have the same drawbacks. Moreover, at a time when business is sluggish and our members are all on the verge of bankruptcy, they will be unable to modify these new wheels to comply with the regulations, which is even more obvious. However, for the benefit of traffic and the public roads, it is certainly necessary to protect them. After careful review by our association, we would like to express the following opinions to your esteemed bureau regarding the modifications: Flat-bed carts should be modified to three and two-eighths-inch angled iron wheels, and rickshaws to two and two-eighths-inch angled iron wheels. This would both maintain road protection and not hinder the work of cart owners or increase their burden, this is one. Regarding the weight limit for rickshaws, we request that it remain as stipulated in 1925, which stated that a single person could carry 500 pounds and two people could carry 1,000 pounds, which is more suitable and reasonable, this is two. We have always admired your bureau's concern for the hardships of laborers, and we hope that you will adopt, reconsider, and amend these measures for implementation. We would be very grateful. Sincerely, to the General Manager of the Municipal Council."

Requesting No Unwarranted Expulsion of Vehicles

The Shanghai Flat-Bed Cart and Rickshaw Industry Mutual Aid Society also sent a letter to the Lao Zha Police Station yesterday, stating: "Respectfully, we have recently learned that more than twenty rickshaw owners, including Zhang Li Fu and others from the Huichang Association, have reported to our association that, at around 10:00 AM today, while they were resting in the open space in front of the Zhongnan Hotel at the intersection of Edward Road and Hubei Road, they were suddenly expelled without cause by Chinese Constable 1956, and one rickshaw belonging to Zhang Li Fu was detained and sent to the police station, accused of obstructing traffic and fined. This is causing insecurity and livelihood problems. We are requesting that you negotiate with the police station to prevent further unwarranted expulsion and to release the detained vehicles so that they can make a living. After investigation, the open space in front of the Zhongnan Hotel is quite large, and parking vehicles does not obstruct traffic. Cart owners have been parking here for many years and it should not be considered a restricted area. Moreover, since the Municipal Council has not announced a prohibition on parking, it should not be rashly expelled and arrested. If this is considered obstructing traffic, then our flat-bed cart and rickshaw industry will have nowhere to go. This concerns the livelihood of laborers. We dare to ask your esteemed police station to understand the difficulties of the times, immediately release the detained vehicles, and allow cart owners to continue parking and resting in the open space in front of the Zhongnan Hotel, so as to prevent accidents caused by high pressure. We would be very grateful. Sincerely, to the Lao Zha Police Station." It is reported that the police station released the detained vehicle after receiving the letter and allowed the cart owners to continue parking and resting in the original location.

Another Case of Child Abuse: Mistress's Cruel Methods

Left Arm of Maid Tied Securely with White Cloth; Right Arm Curled Up, Tied Securely, and Stitched Shut

Li Shaoping, a Cantonese residing on the upper floor of No. 9, Lane 7, Deqing Lane, Muir Road in this city, and his wife, Li Lu, purchased two maids last year, Chun Mei, age eleven, and Lai Xi, age seven, both from Danyang. Li Shaoping runs a tea shop in Hongkou, leaving early and returning late. Li Lu is addicted to mahjong and also goes out frequently. She often beat and abused the two maids, Chun Mei and Lai Xi. On the 3rd of this month (December), a righteous person reported the case to the Chinese Child Welfare Association. The Association immediately sent Zhao Jian, a staff member from the Protection Group, together with Western Detective Harvey and Chinese Detectives Li Wenzhao and Wang Shanqing from the Chengdu Road Police Station, to investigate. Upon entering the room, they saw that Chun Mei had already been tied to the bed leg by Li Lu with a strip of white cloth on her left arm. Her right arm was curled up, tied securely, and stitched shut, making her unable to move from the kneeling position on the ground. Furthermore, she had told the girl that if she tried to stand up and accidentally damaged the stitching, she would be beaten to death. At that time, Western Detective Harvey ordered her to stand up, but the maid did not dare to, fearing that she would be beaten to death by her mistress. Li Shaoping and Li Lu were not at home. The female servant, Pan Xishi, and the two maids were taken to Guangren Hospital for examination. According to the examination, the maid had injuries on her head and arms and was very pitiful. They were immediately taken to the police station for handling. Subsequently, the female servant, Pan Xishi, testified and the two maids confessed that they were often abused by their mistress, Li Lu. Yesterday (the 4th) at 9:00 AM, the female servant, Pan Xishi, and the two maids were escorted to the First Special District Court for questioning. According to the two young maids' testimony, the perpetrators were not present. The court ordered that the two maids be sent to the Jiliang Asylum for care and will be dealt with when Li Shaoping and his wife are detained.

Widow Dies Miserably After Abortion for Affair with Uncle

Court Sends Personnel for Autopsy Yesterday; Paramour and Midwife Arrested

Wang Lu, a local widow residing at No. 1, Lane 62, Route Lafayette in the French Concession, is 37 years old. Her husband died more than ten years ago. She has a small amount of assets and vowed to remain a widow. Because she had no children, she adopted a daughter this year, who is fifteen years old. Unexpectedly, although Mrs. Lu is old, she still has charm. Starting a year ago, she suddenly became unwilling to live alone and started an affair with a distant uncle, Wang Xinggen (32 years old this year, with one lame leg, works as a track lever worker No. 34 in the French tram company, usually stationed at the entrance of Baoanfang, Xinqiao Street to manage the shifting of trams on lines 5 and 6). The two became intimate. To facilitate his work, Wang Xinggen rented a spare room from a Ningbo tailor, Li Changgen, at No. 4, Baoanfang, Xinqiao Street, as his residence. Since Wang Xinggen rented a residence outside, Wang Lu took the opportunity to claim that she was going to her mother's home on Hongqiao Road in Shanghai to help take care of her younger brother's wife who was giving birth, as there were too many people in her own home and it was inappropriate. She went to Wang Xinggen's residence for a rendezvous and stayed overnight before going home. Who knew that after several encounters, a fetus had secretly formed in her womb, which had been four months. Her abdomen gradually increased in size. Fearing being exposed, she secretly discussed the matter with her paramour Wang Xinggen. On the morning of the 27th of last month, Wang Xinggen accompanied her to a midwife in Fa Hua Town, north of Xujiahui in western Shanghai, to request an abortion. Mrs. Lu first claimed at home that her younger brother's wife was giving birth and she had to go back to help take care of her. After leaving the house, she went to the paramour's residence. After the midwife gave her medicine, the fetus was aborted. Unexpectedly, the inside was injured. Medical treatment was ineffective. At 1:30 PM on the 3rd, she died in the paramour Wang Xinggen's residence. Wang, seeing the disaster, was at a loss. Therefore, the second landlord, Li Changgen, inquired Wang Xinggen to find out the location of Mrs. Lu's family and went to notify her husband's younger brother, Wang Guanjin, (31 years old this year, previously worked in the Sanitation Department of the French Municipal Council, now works as an accountant at the Republic Automobile Company at 549 Edward Road). He heard that his sister-in-law was helping to take care of her younger brother's wife who was giving birth, and her body was healthy when she left. Why did she suddenly die in Xinqiao Street? He was very strange. First, he went to her mother's house to inquire. They said that she went home the next day and there was nothing unusual. Guanjin then rushed to No. 4, Baoanfang, Xinqiao Street to check and learned that Mrs. Lu had been having an affair with her uncle Wang Xinggen for more than a year and recently died from an abortion due to pregnancy. Wang Guanjin was shocked when he learned the truth and immediately reported to the French Police Station in charge, and sent detective Bu Zhenglong to arrest the adulterer Wang Xinggen. At the same time, the body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan branch for autopsy. Yesterday at noon, he reported to the Second Special Court. Prosecutor Wang Ren and forensic medical officers arrived at the scene, and it was verified that Wang Lu died from an abortion. The case investigator reported the investigation. The official asked Wang Guanjin a question and ordered the body to be handed over to Wang Guanjin for burial. One side, the detective and Wang Xinggen rushed to Fa Hua to find the midwife who performed the abortion and reported to the local Public Security Bureau for assistance to arrest the midwife and take her back to the police station for detention. Today, he will be taken to the Second Special Court for trial along with Wang Xinggen.

Municipal Government Held the Fifth Mass Wedding Ceremony Yesterday

One Hundred and Eleven Couples Participating; Solemn Ceremony, Good Order

The city's fifth mass wedding ceremony was held at 3:00 PM yesterday in the City Hall Auditorium. The ceremony was grand, and the order was good. Originally there were a total of one hundred and twelve couples, but one couple, number 24, was unable to participate due to unforeseen circumstances. Therefore, there were only one hundred and eleven couples. The details are as follows.

Auditorium Decoration

Previous mass wedding ceremonies were all held in the large auditorium in the city center, which is both grand and magnificent. This year's ceremony was also held there. The decorations and arrangements were the same as before. In the center, the wedding candles burned brightly. The stage was decorated with festive ribbons. The seats for the officiant and the master of ceremonies were separated. The right corner of the auditorium was the piano seat. Both sides were the entrances and exits for guests. The right corner in front of the main entrance was the military band playing music.

Solemn Wedding Ceremony

The wedding ceremony began at 3:25 PM. First, the master of ceremonies, Wang Xianqing, reported the points to note for the guests. Then, the military band played the wedding march. The new couples walked slowly into the auditorium in order, led by Sun Yongyi and Yan Wenkai, staff members of the Social Affairs Bureau. The ceremony began. First, the married couples stood at attention. Next, they paid the highest respects to the Party and National Flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen. Third, the wedding vows were read. Fourth, the new couples stood facing each other to salute. Fifth, the marriage certificates and souvenirs were presented to the new couples. The new couples came forward in order to receive them. Sixth, the officiant gave a speech. Seventh, the new couples bowed to thank the officiant. The ceremony was completed. Originally, there were a total of one hundred and twelve couples, but one couple, number 24, was unable to participate due to unforeseen circumstances. Therefore, the actual number of couples participating in yesterday's wedding ceremony was one hundred and eleven.

Representative Officiation

Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Social Affairs Bureau Director Wu Xingya were attending the First Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee in Nanjing and were unable to return. Therefore, Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and Social Affairs Bureau Secretary Li Suixian represented the two officiants, presenting marriage certificates and souvenirs to the married couples. The Mayor's representative gave a speech, and the Social Affairs Bureau Director's representative read the wedding vows, declaring the marriage legal. The ceremony was extremely quick and solemn as the new couples had practiced the ceremony very thoroughly the day before. The ceremony lasted 35 minutes and the good order was more prominent than in previous sessions.

Sixth Session Registration

After the ceremony, registration for the sixth mass wedding ceremony will begin next Monday (the 9th of this month). The number of couples will still be limited to one hundred. The announcement of approval will be from January 10th to 12th. The wedding ceremony will be held on February 5th next spring.

Destitute and Helpless: Mother and Son Commit Suicide Together

Mother Addicted to Opium Survives, Son Unable to Resist and Dies

Zhao Wen, a woman from Ningbo, 45 years old this year, married Zhao, a native of the area outside Ximen in Yin County, as a concubine in her early years, and gave birth to a son named Zu'en, 22 years old this year. After Zhao and his first wife died one after another, Zhao Wen discriminated against the eldest son born to the first wife, who was expelled at the age of fifteen. From then on, all the inherited property fell into Zhao Wen's hands. Mrs. Zhao became addicted to smoking and indulged in opium. She did not educate or teach her own son, and let him roam freely. In a few years, the meagre legacy was squandered. Her eldest son, Zuyi, was expelled to Shanghai, completed his apprenticeship, worked diligently in business, and developed year by year, married and started a family. He is now over forty and works as a clerk at the Gold Exchange, residing at No. 198, Xiangfu Lane, Carter Road. The mother and son of Mrs. Zhao ran out of property in their hometown and eked out a living as vendors. Recently, Mrs. Zhao's physical strength has declined with age, so she quit her addiction and stopped working because she could not do it anymore. Her son Zu'en also had no capital to make a living, so the mother and son were always worried and had no face to see her eldest son and daughter-in-law to ask for help. Also, because the weather was getting colder, their clothes were thin, and they were starving. They wandered to Shanghai and could not find a way to make a living. The mother and son committed suicide on the 2nd at night. They bought four boxes of raw opium worth two jiao a box with their remaining capital. That night at 11 o'clock, they went to the Xinxin Hotel at No. 138, West Zilai Huo Street in the French Concession. The mother and son used aliases. Zhao Zu'en changed his name to Zhao A Da and Mrs. Zhao changed her name to Wang Wen. They checked into Room 10 on the pretext of borrowing a room to stay overnight, and swallowed half of the four boxes of raw opium each to commit suicide. After taking the poison, Zu'en wrote a suicide note in pencil to the hotel owner and newspaper reporters, stating that the mother and son committed suicide at the same time because of the long period of poverty due to the brother not providing assistance. After his death, please notify his brother to buy two coffins for burial. After writing, he lay on the bed waiting to die. By the afternoon of the next day, Zu'en died from the poison. Mrs. Zhao was originally an addict and could resist the force of two boxes of opium, which was not enough to kill her. By 6:00 PM the next evening, Mrs. Zhao woke up from the poison and saw that her son was dead, but she had not died. Seeing her son's tragic state, she couldn't help but cry loudly in the room. The tea room waiter Tan Fuxian went upstairs to inquire and learned that the mother and son had taken poison and the son had died. He immediately reported to the French Police Station and sent detectives to investigate. Mrs. Zhao cried and refused to tell the reason for the suicide. Later, a suicide note was found, and the body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan branch for an autopsy. Zhao Wen was taken to the police station. According to the address on the suicide note, her eldest son Zhao Zuyi was notified, and his wife Zhao Wang came to the police station for questioning. After questioning, they learned that Mrs. Zhao and her son committed suicide in the world, and ordered Mrs. Wang to take her concubine home. At first, Mrs. Wang refused to take her, but after the detective's persuasion, Mrs. Zhao was taken away and went to the autopsy station the next day to wait for the hearing to collect the body. Yesterday, the police reported to the Second Special Court, and Prosecutor Wang Ren and the medical examiner arrived at the station at noon to verify that Zhao Zu'en, Zhao A Da, committed suicide by poisoning. The body was handed over to Zhao Wang and Zhao Wen for burial.

The Chief of the 60th Division's Communications Office Embezzles Over 70,000 Yuan, Flees to Shanghai with a Prostitute for a Life of Pleasure, Then Meets Another Prostitute and Spends Money Like Water, Enjoying Himself Immensely, Truly Embodying the Spirit of "Amassing Hundreds of Thousands and Riding a Crane to Yangzhou," but the Revelry Is Short-Lived as the Crime Is Discovered and He Is Arrested

Lin Chengwei, a Guangdong native, currently twenty-two years old, served as the chief of the Sichuan communications office of the 16th Division of the National Revolutionary Army. On the 28th of last month, Lin stole a seal belonging to Pan Wei-fu, the chief of the division's quartermaster department, in Chengdu, Sichuan, along with a blank check. After fraudulently obtaining 76,000 yuan from the Chengdu branch of the China Farmers' Bank, he immediately purchased two plane tickets on the 30th of the same month with a Sichuan woman named Wang Yuqing (age 19), using the alias Liu Sheng. They flew to Shanghai, renting room 309 at the Great Eastern Hotel on Yinghua Street, Nanjing Road, in the Public Concession, still using the name Liu Sheng. However, Lin Chengwei, having

Embezzled a Huge Sum,

deposited 50,000 yuan in the Juxingcheng Bank on Jiujiang Road. He kept the rest close by, spending it recklessly, indulging in the pleasures of theaters, dance halls, and women all day long. He believed he was beyond the reach of the law and could live happily ever after. Guo Shengzhao, a tea boy at the hotel, seeing Lin's extravagance and lavish spending, regarded him as a wealthy benefactor and became obsequious, even introducing him to a local prostitute named Jiang Yueying to keep him company, agreeing on a daily fee of 20 yuan. Lin, finding Jiang

Quite Beautiful, Was Pleased.

In addition to renting room 429 at the Nanjing Hotel on Shanxi Road as a place to enjoy himself with Jiang, he also rented a car, number 18017, from the Huali Motor Company nearby for transportation, to show off his wealth, paying 18 yuan per day in car fare. He and Jiang went out to play together, and to please Jiang, he bought her a gold bracelet and a diamond-studded platinum watch as gifts. He enjoyed himself immensely, showing off his wealth. Unexpectedly, Lin's actions had been exposed in Sichuan, discovered by Pan Wei-fu, the chief of the quartermaster department, who

Telegraphed the Division's

office in Nanjing. The director of that office, Wu Xiangrong, reported to Chen Pei, the commander of the 60th Division, who ordered a strict search. At the same time, he checked with the Chengdu branch of the China Aviation Corporation and confirmed that a person named Liu Sheng, accompanied by a woman, had flown to Shanghai. Director Wu then tracked them to Shanghai and reported to the Shanghai Municipal Police, requesting assistance in the investigation. He also worked with Huang Peilin, the head of the detective team, and detectives Gao Quchuan and Cai Baotai, first investigating at Hongqiao Airport, where it was confirmed that Liu Sheng had arrived in Shanghai by plane. They then began a secret search of the various

Hotels in the Foreign Concession.

Until the night before last, when they searched the Great Eastern Hotel and found a person named Liu Sheng in room 309. However, at that time, they learned that Lin was with Jiang and the tea boy Guo Shengzhao, watching a play at the Grand Guangming Theater on Jing'an Temple Road. At 11 p.m., they cooperated with Ding Huaguo, a Chinese detective from the Xinzha Patrol Station, and arrested Lin Chengwei, Jiang Yueying, and Guo Shengzhao at the entrance of the Grand Guangming. They found 4,113.40 yuan in cash on Lin, as well as a

Bank Draft for 50,000 Yuan

from the Shanghai Juxingcheng Bank.

They also arrested Wang Yuqing at the Great Eastern Hotel. During the search, they found 14,850 yuan in cash in her suitcase, as well as Pan Wei-fu's seal and the gold bracelet and watch on Jiang's person. All were taken to the Xinzha Patrol Station. After investigation by the chief, Jiang Yueying and Guo Shengzhao were found to be uninvolved and were released. Lin and Wang were detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Zhang Tianyin, the patrol station's lawyer, stated the above facts and did not oppose the Shanghai Municipal Police's request

To Transfer the Case.

According to Wu Xiangrong, the director of the 60th Division's Nanjing office, and a detective from the Shanghai Municipal Police who had turned himself in, a request was made to transfer the case. When questioned, Lin Chengwei confessed that he had committed the crime in Sichuan with a woman named Li Yueying, who received 1,500 yuan. However, he claimed that Wang Yuqing was a prostitute from Sichuan and knew nothing about the matter. Judge Wu Zehan briefly questioned Wang and then ordered that Lin Chengwei be handed over to the Shanghai Municipal Police detectives to be taken back. The evidence was also transferred. Wang Yuqing was also allowed to be handed over to the Shanghai Municipal Police to be taken back.

Defaulting on Goods Delivered and Pawned, the Store Announces Liquidation, and Ye Chuanhan and Others Surrender to the Patrol Station and Are Detained.

Ye Chuanhan and Yu Lanxin, natives of Ningbo, jointly opened the Qiafeng Department Store at No. 7, Donghuali, Tangshan Road. Recently, they had ordered goods worth 1,452.06 yuan from the Yisheng Weaving Factory at No. 47, Yongchengli, East Broadway Road, and goods worth 312 yuan from the Rongji Store in Yongfengfang, North Sichuan Road. After Ye and others obtained the goods, they pawned them at various pawnshops to convert them into cash. On the first of this month, they announced liquidation. The Yisheng Factory and others reported the matter to the Huishan Patrol Station. Chinese Detective Cai Liu and Detective Xu Decheng investigated. The day before yesterday, Ye and Yu, accompanied by a lawyer, surrendered to the patrol station and were detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Fifth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Jiang Baolian, the patrol station's lawyer, stated that the two defendants, Ye and Yu, had never ordered more than 100 yuan worth of goods from Yisheng and others before. However, starting from October 20th, they continuously ordered goods, up to four times. The value of the goods from Yisheng exceeded 1,400 yuan, and the value of the goods from Rongji also exceeded 300 yuan. In addition, there were five or six other businesses from which goods had been obtained, with a total value of about 4,000 yuan. The defendants pawned goods worth over 3,000 yuan for over 1,000 yuan. The pawn tickets were taken away by a Zhao Yongkang, who has been detained by the French Concession police for fraud. As the case requires detailed investigation, no charges have been filed, and a request is made to allow detention. The lawyer hired by Ye and others stated that the liquidation of Qiafeng was due to the inability to maintain operations and that there was no fraud. On the 26th of last month, over 1,600 yuan was paid for goods. If there was intent to defraud, why not close down before the 20th, which would have resulted in an additional profit of over 1,000 yuan, rather than going bankrupt on the first of this month, and so on. Judge Zhan Liangce briefly questioned Ye and Yu and ordered that the case be heard again in a week.

China Longji Flour Mill Announces Liquidation

China Longji Flour Mill, due to poor business and financial difficulties, announced liquidation on Monday of this week. The factory was established in June of the 11th year of the Republic of China. In January of the 13th year, it underwent internal reorganization. In October of the 15th year, it was renamed Fengji, and last May, it was renamed Longji. When the factory was established, its capital was 250,000 yuan. The factory was located in Tanziawan, Zhabei, and the distribution office was located at No. 1 and 2, Tianzhutang Street. The manager, Zhou Jingzhi, was a native of Chaozhou and a leader in the Chaozhou grain and flour industry. He was also the chairman of Zhengming Bank. The deputy manager was Chen Ganting, and the shareholders were Ding Houqing, Ge Huanzhang, and others. After the reorganization in the 15th year, the capital was changed from 250,000 yuan to 120,000 yuan. Last year, losses reached 150,000 to 160,000 yuan, and the shareholders had no intention of continuing operations. In May of this year, it was reorganized, and Zhou Jingzhi took over independently. Within a few months, another 30,000 yuan was lost. Therefore, it announced closure three days ago. Now, as there is no way to continue operations, liquidation has been announced.

The China Critic Weekly Publishes a Special Issue on Rural Construction

The English China Critic Weekly, founded by scholars Gui Zhongshu, Zhu Shaoping, Liu Dajun, Lin Yutang, and others in the 17th year of the Republic of China, has been in existence for eight years, making it the oldest English weekly magazine run by Chinese people. Its impartial commentary and rich content have long been praised by Chinese and foreigners. Recently, in view of the bankruptcy of China's rural areas and to draw the attention of Chinese and foreigners, the magazine has specially compiled a special issue on rural construction, which was published yesterday. The contents include "China's Rural Problems," "Our Country's Improvement of Rural Areas," and "The Rural Rehabilitation Committee's Progress on Rural Construction." Each issue is still sold for 20 cents, without any price increase. The annual subscription is 7 yuan, and the half-year subscription is 4 yuan. Students can subscribe for half price with a school seal as proof, as a special offer. The distribution office is located at the China Critic Weekly, Jing'an Building, 749 Jing'an Temple Road, Shanghai, and in various Chinese and foreign bookstores and book bureaus in various provinces.

The Trial of the Tang Akun Murder Case Concludes

Tang Akun, a local resident living at No. 491, Kangnaotuo Road, West Shanghai, was walking with his friend Yan Shengquan near the Yan Family House on Difeng Road last winter when he was hacked to death with an ax. Later, the family of the deceased filed a complaint with the prosecutor's office of the local court, stating that Tang Akun was murdered by Yan Shengjing, who had arranged for Zhao Arer and others to wait for him on the road. The court, after receiving the complaint, ordered the arrest of the criminals, but they could not be found. Recently, Yan secretly returned to Shanghai and was sent to the local court by the police. After investigation by Prosecutor Xie, it was determined that he was guilty of murder and prosecuted in the criminal court. Judge Wu Deying has presided over several trials, but the case has not been concluded, as detailed in previous reports. It is learned that the case was heard again yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM by Judge Wu. Tang Jishi, the plaintiff, appeared in court and stated that the deceased was her husband and requested that the law be enforced and that private compensation of 7,600 yuan be sought. Yan Shengquan, who was in custody, vehemently denied the allegations, insisting that he had been framed. Then, Gu Tangshi, the sister of the deceased, appeared in court and stated that since her brother had been murdered, Tang Jishi had filed a complaint. She had not joined at first. At the previous hearing, her sister-in-law (Tang Jishi) said that a man named Yong Agen, who claimed to be her brother's uncle, had come to investigate, so she also came to participate today. Before his death, her brother Akun had no children and had adopted her son Shunlin as his heir. As for Tang Agen, he was a distant uncle. Tang Agen testified, requesting justice for his nephew. Finally, the witness Zhang Bulin appeared in court and testified. At this point, Prosecutor Xie appeared in court to present his arguments. Then, the lawyer Sha Xunyi, hired by the defendant, rose to defend him for a long time. The judge considered the hearing to be concluded and scheduled the sentencing. The defendant was returned to custody.

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the tenants of Hongfu Lane on North Henan Road petitioned the Municipal Rent Reduction Association to negotiate due to high rents. Disturbance at the Da Hu Hotel Last Night

Gathering in a Room and Teasing Women, Ignoring Warnings and Beating Up the Inspector

A guest checked into a room at the Da Hu Hotel on Dongxinqiao Street in the French Concession yesterday afternoon. The hotel assigned him room 411 on the fourth floor. In the evening, a large group of men came to the room, shouting and making a lot of noise. The hotel was afraid that the people were too mixed and would cause trouble, so they instructed the tea boys to pay extra attention. At around 9:30 PM, three men in plain clothes were loitering in the lobby of the floor, teasing women coming in and out. The tea boys felt that this was offensive to public morals and tried to persuade them to stop. Unexpectedly, the three men not only refused but even made things difficult for the tea boys and went straight up to the sixth floor, automatically breaking into room 608, which caused a commotion. The accountant downstairs heard the noise and ordered Sun Zhaobei, the hotel's inspector, to go upstairs to mediate. However, the men continued to act unreasonably and ran back to room 411, calling the others in the room to rush to the lobby. They attacked the inspector without asking questions, causing Sun Zhaobei to be beaten. Seeing this, the accountant urgently notified the Daziwuzhong Patrol Station, which sent detectives to the scene and arrested all those who had caused the trouble, including Xue Hesheng, Hu Yigong, and others, totaling six people. After questioning by the patrol station, they were transferred to the Lujiawan Patrol Station on the grounds that the case involved a mob causing trouble and disrupting public order, and were scheduled to be sent to court this morning. The injured inspector, Sun Zhaobei, was sent to Renji Hospital for examination and treatment.

The Dongya Paint Factory Creates National Lithopone

Lithopone is the English name for lithopone, commonly known as "foreign zinc white," which is a major raw material for paints, coatings, painted cloth, and rubber. Its use is very broad. The goods have been imported from overseas, and the outflow of money is alarming. Gao Enhong, the former Minister of Communications, in view of this, gathered comrades to establish the Dongya Paint Factory to manufacture Taiji brand lithopone from domestic raw materials. Through long-term research and gradual refinement, it has surpassed imported products. The goods are divided into six grades: 12 degrees, 15 degrees, 22 degrees, 30 degrees, 40 degrees, and 50 degrees. The grades are very accurate, and the powder is very fine and white, which is in line with the needs of the industrial community. It is truly an excellent and complete national product. Now, the factory has entrusted the Tongrenhe Paint Sundries Store at No. 80, Minguo Road, as the sole distributor for promotion. It is heard that the Tongrenhe Store was established more than 80 years ago and is the pioneer of the paint and sundries industry. It also has a branch, Tongtaixiang, on Minguo Road, which has a history of more than 30 years. The store is famous far and wide for its complete range of styles and fair prices. In the past, it sold Tiger brand lithopone manufactured by a German factory, which had a wide sales network. Now, in order to promote national goods, it also sells Dongya lithopone. The factory has promoted the right people, and its future achievements will be remarkable, which is also a blessing for national goods.

No Right Turns at the Lloyd Road Intersection

Article 46, Section 3 of the Municipal Council's Traffic Regulations regarding the method of driving at the Nanjing Road-Lloyd Road intersection has been revised and will be implemented from the 16th of this month. From that date, all vehicles at that location, regardless of the direction of travel, will not be allowed to turn right during certain hours of the day. The specified hours are 8:00 AM to 9:30 AM, 12:00 PM to 12:30 PM, 1:30 PM to 2:30 PM, and 4:30 PM to 6:00 PM, except on Sundays and public holidays.

Letter to the Editor

To the Editor,

I have read the article in the "Local News" section of your newspaper on the 3rd of this month entitled "Kangti Road Vegetable Vendors Provisionally Allowed to Set Up Stalls by the French Concession Public Works Department." It includes the following passage: "The stallholders publicly elected three representatives, including Zhou Wenxian, to bring a petition to Mr. Lu Bohong of the Chinese Directorate. Mr. Lu personally met with them and immediately telephoned the French Concession Public Works Department to discuss the matter with Director Wei Zhiren. The department agreed to temporarily allow the vendors to set up stalls before the market is built to provide relief, etc." This is not in accordance with the facts.

On the 2nd of this month, representatives of the Kangti Road vegetable vendors came to petition. I telephoned Director Wei to ask how to handle the matter. Director Wei replied that the case should be handled by the relevant police station. I immediately informed the representatives accordingly. There was no mention of "agreeing to temporarily allow the vendors to set up stalls before the market is built to provide relief." I am deeply concerned that this might cause confusion. Therefore, I am writing to request a correction.

Sincerely,

Lu Bohong

December 4, 24

Overview of the Shanghai Cotton Fabric Industry (Continued)

Compiled by the China Credit Bureau (No. 4 of Shanghai Industry and Commerce Overview)

4. Analysis of the Sharp Decline in Foreign Imports

Since the opening of trade, the amount of foreign cotton fabric imported has increased year by year, consistently ranking first among all imports. However, in the past eight years, the import figures for cotton fabric have shown a downward trend. In 1926, cotton fabric still held the top position among imports, totaling 268.1 million national currency. From 1930, it fell to second place, totaling 102.2 million national currency. It maintained its original position in 1931, but the amount decreased to 167.1 million national currency. In 1932, it further dropped to third place, totaling 110 million national currency. In 1933, it dropped to seventh place, totaling 58.2 million national currency. In 1934, it fell below tenth place, totaling 13.1 million national currency. The import of cotton fabric, in the span of eight years, dropped from first place to below tenth place, with the amount decreasing sharply from 268.1 million national currency to 13.1 million national currency. Therefore, many people are gleeful, believing that our country's cotton weaving industry has made considerable progress. However, upon closer examination, we should not be overly optimistic. The sharp decline in cotton fabric imports is due to the following two major reasons, in addition to the genuine progress made by the national textile industry.

(1) The Sharp Increase in Foreign Factories in China. As capitalism develops to the stage of imperialism, its economic aggression towards colonies and semi-colonies has further shifted from "commodity export" to "capital export." Since Britain and Japan have already occupied a considerable advantage in China's cotton fabric market and have also obtained concession privileges, it is inevitable that they will set up factories in China. Setting up factories locally allows them to utilize cheap Chinese labor, reduce tariffs and transportation costs, and lower the cost of cotton fabric to a minimum in order to increase their sales power. According to statistics, the most textile factories set up by Britain and Japan in China are in Shanghai. There are three British factories and thirty Japanese factories. Their scale and capital are far beyond the reach of Chinese factories. According to the figures surveyed by the Chinese Cotton Mill Owners Association in March of this year, the comparison is as follows:

Percentage Occupied by Chinese Factories Percentage Occupied by Japanese Factories Percentage Occupied by British Factories Total

Looms 47.96 45.90 6.14 100

Based on the above table, the number of looms in Chinese factories is already less than that in Japanese factories, which shows the erosion of Chinese factories and the continuous progress of Japanese factories in recent years. As foreign factories in China become increasingly developed, cotton fabric imports may see a sharp decline, but the outflow of our country's resources remains the same.

(2) Decline in Purchasing Power. Cotton fabric is the main clothing material for Chinese civilians. The increase or decrease in cotton fabric consumption reflects the rise and fall of civilian life. In recent years, the rural economy has collapsed, cities have declined, and civilians are struggling with poverty and cannot even afford food, let alone clothing. Therefore, the purchasing power of cotton fabric has been greatly reduced. The output of local factories is already greater than the demand, and foreign imports must be drastically reduced. The import numbers of cotton fabric from Shanghai in the past three years are listed for comparison as follows. (Unit: 1,000 Customs Gold Units)

Port 1932 Percentage 1933 Percentage 1934 Percentage

Shanghai 17,062 27.68 13,600 45.60 6,953 51.01

Other 44,566 72.32 16,222 54.40 6,678 48.99

Total 61,628 100.00 29,822 100.00 13,631 100.00

From the above table, it can be observed that cotton fabric imports have decreased year by year in Shanghai and other ports, and the degree of decrease is more severe in other ports than in Shanghai. This indicates that the decline in consumption power of civilians in the interior is more drastic than in the coastal provinces.

In addition, the fall of the four northeastern provinces has also led to a sharp decline in our country's cotton fabric import volume. Since the "September 18th" incident, the northeastern market has been exclusively occupied by Japanese goods, eliminating the need for re-export through Tianjin and Shanghai.

5. Inventory Situation

The cotton fabric industry in Shanghai mainly deals in machine-woven cotton fabric. Its sources of inventory have changed considerably over the years. In the past, it relied heavily on foreign firms that engaged in import businesses. In recent years, as textile and dyeing factories have become increasingly developed in this city and neighboring counties, locally produced goods have been sufficient to meet the needs. Therefore, the sources of inventory are significantly different from before. According to statistics from the Shanghai Cotton Fabric Industry Association, in the first half of this year, approximately 95% of the inventory came from textile and dyeing factories, and approximately 5% came from foreign firms engaged in import businesses. The breakdown by country of origin is as follows:

(1) Domestic Goods. This year, the average daily sales of domestically produced plain cotton fabric in the city's cotton fabric industry during the first half of the year were approximately 10,000 pieces, and the sales of colored fabric were approximately 3,000 to 4,000 pieces. Compared with the same period last year, some decreased by 10-20%, and others decreased by 20-30%. As of May of this year, the city's inventory was approximately 34,000 to 35,000 pieces of plain cotton fabric and 22,000 to 23,000 pieces of colored fabric.

(2) Western Goods. As of May of this year, Shanghai only imported approximately 3,000 pieces of Western goods. Among them, foreign yarn and linen yarn accounted for approximately 500-600 pieces, poplin and tarpaulin accounted for approximately 200 pieces, bleached cloth, Western satin, feather satin, red labels, and printed cloth accounted for approximately 1,400 pieces, flannel accounted for approximately 400-500 pieces, and grey cloth and muslin accounted for approximately 200-300 pieces. If we include the unsold inventory from the previous year, the city's total inventory is approximately 3,000 pieces. The total sales volume is only one-tenth of that in 1932, and the rate of decline is truly alarming. In addition to the existing inventory of more than 2,000 pieces, Shanghai imported approximately 200 pieces of Russian printed cloth this spring. However, the lightweight cloth produced by the British-owned Ewo Cotton Mill in China is still selling in the market, with a daily output of approximately 200 pieces and an inventory of more than 4,000 pieces in Shanghai.

(3) Japanese Goods. Since the increase in customs duties last year, Japanese goods such as five-branch worsted cloth, single-ply serge, and printed cloth have no longer been imported. However, printed goods such as colored jacquard, printed jacquard, star flannel, modern crepe, snowflake small-grid serge, and mass-market goods such as plain feather satin, eight-piece satin-faced jacquard, eight-piece jacquard satin, double-width umbrella-faced feather satin, Zhongshan flannel, plain foreign yarn, moon velvet, and cotton flannel are still imported, totaling approximately 12,000 to 13,000 pieces. It is also said that Japanese merchants are cutting the original pieces of cotton fabric into smaller pieces and declaring them as remnants for import in order to reduce customs duties. In recent years, this type of remnants has flooded the markets in northern China. The general public is competing to buy them because of their low prices. This trend is also increasing in the southern ports. If no measures are taken to curb this, its impact on the future of domestic cloth will be significant. As for the products manufactured in Shanghai factories, in addition to five-branch jacquard, single-ply serge, bleached cloth, coarse cloth, market cloth, printed cloth, eight-sided cloth, and printed jacquard, the most common are muslin, twill, and unbleached cloth. The daily output is approximately 20,000 pieces, and the inventory in Shanghai is approximately 10,000 pieces. (To be continued)

—Total Donation Fund of 160,000 Yuan—

Subsidizing High School and University Students Unable to Afford Education. Rewarding Academic Research and Those with Special Inventions

Chinese and History Textbooks for Primary and Secondary Schools Will Be Revised to Avoid Hindering Diplomatic Relations

(Special Dispatch from Peiping) The educational circles in Peiping are affected by the current situation. Some university students have requested leave, and some have staged city tours. Although the principals of various schools have repeatedly advised them, it is difficult to cope with the environment. Lei Sichang, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, has decided to automatically revise the Chinese and history textbooks for primary and secondary schools to express the intention of not hindering diplomatic relations. The situation of each party is recorded as follows:

Telegram from Educational Leaders

The principals of various universities in Peiping and leaders of the educational and cultural circles have issued a telegram expressing their attitude towards the current situation. The original telegram is recorded as follows: "Recently, newspapers in Peiping and Tianjin have published articles openly claiming that there is public opinion in North China demanding autonomy or self-determination. This is sufficient to confuse the public. What we have personally seen and heard is that, apart from a few villains on the street who have been used by others to issue leaflets and fabricate public opinion, the people of all circles have no intention of breaking away from the Central Government and seeking autonomy. We hope that the government and the people of the country will not be deceived. We especially hope that the central government and the authorities in Peiping, Tianjin, and Hebei will eliminate the source of chaos and use all their strength to maintain the integrity of the country's territory and administration." Xu Songming, Li Zheng, Jiang Menglin, Mei Yiqi, Lu Zhiwei, Hu Shi, Fu Sinian, Yuan Tongli, Tao Mengzhi, Liu Yunchou, Liu Tingfang, Yang Likui, Wu Wenzao, Zha Liangzhao, Zhang Xiruo, Zhou Binglin, Jiang Tingfu, and dozens of others.

The students are naturally worried about the urgency of the situation. At this time of crisis, the actions of university students must be more cautious. Any opinions can be discussed with the school at any time to maintain close contact. Do not take any rash actions that may lead to unexpected disputes. At this critical time, if students have any opinions, they must consult with the school and take responsibility together. Thoughts and actions must be calm and cool to get through this crisis.

Children's Education Novel

Little Boy

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Another long trek in the quickly deepening twilight, another deep disappointment, because when they reached the tree, they saw that it was not the one Neidai had climbed before. Looking around, they could not find a path.

"Are we lost?" Robert asked with a trembling voice. In despair, he couldn't help but hug his little bucket tighter.

"Not too bad yet. I just don't know which way to go. I think we should try shouting."

So the two of them shouted together until their throats were hoarse, but there was no response. Only the frogs in the wilderness competed in a chorus of croaking sounds.

Lai tried hard to muster courage, but her heart felt like it was sinking.

"I don't think I can walk anymore; my boots are so heavy, I can't drag them anymore," Robert said, and then sat on a stone, truly exhausted.

"Then we'll just have to stay here all night. I'm not too worried, as long as snakes don't come."

"I'm afraid of snakes. I can't stay here all night. Oh, I really don't want to be lost," Bob said, pouting his face and crying. Suddenly, an idea came to him, so he said with a very confident tone:

"Mommy will come and find me, she always does; I'm not afraid now."

"She won't know where we are."

"She didn't know I was locked in the icehouse, but she found me. I know she will come," Robert replied, saying it so confidently that Nan'en felt a lot more relieved, just sitting by his side, but still couldn't help but regret it, sighing and saying:

"We really shouldn't have wandered off."

Yesterday's Inter-University Cross-Country Race: Fudan Wins Championship, Jinan Second, Guanghua Absent Yesterday, Jinan's Li Jiqing First Individually

The Jiangda Sports Association's 9th Cross-Country Race was held at National Jinan University in Zhenru at 12:00 noon yesterday. Guanghua withdrew due to circumstances. Only Jinan and Fudan participated. As a result, Jinan's Li Qingji finished first with a time of 18 minutes and 20 seconds, and Fudan also won the championship with a strong team. In total, Fudan scored 32 points and Jinan scored 46 points. Details are recorded as follows:

A Silver Whistle Signals Athletes Forward

At 12:00 noon yesterday, all team members gathered at the back gate of Jinan University, including seven from Fudan (including No. 4 Zhang Huiyuan, who joined as a guest and was not scored) and six from Jinan. The Jinan Boy Scouts maintained order, led by Chen Bingde leading several Boy Scouts. Shen Kunnan gave the signal, and with a silver whistle, the athletes rushed forward. Yang Qingxie, Lan Shijie, Chen Tianru, and others led the way. The ground was overgrown with weeds, the road was rugged, and there was a lot of accumulated water, so they all dragged through the mud and water. At this time, Lan Shijie quickened his pace and took the lead, followed by Yang Qingxie. Li Jiqing also caught up to third place. The other athletes followed closely behind.

Li Jiqing Bravely Takes the Lead

As they advanced to Gujiazhai, the road gradually became flat. Jinan's Li Qingji began to stand out, catching up from second to first place, and took the lead. When passing Jiaotong Road, Li Qingji was in the lead, Yang Qingxie had passed Lan Shijie and was in second place, and Zheng Boyi was also closely ranked fourth. The distances between each person were very close, only three or four meters apart, while the rest were far behind. Afterwards, Li Qingji ran faster and faster, and Yang Qingxie could not surpass him. Until the front gate of Jinan University, Li finished first with a time of 18 minutes and 20 seconds, Yang Qingxie was second, about 35 feet behind, Lan Shijie was third, and Zheng Boyi was fourth, with similar distances. The fifth place and beyond were far behind.

Fudan Wins This Year's Championship

The referee at the finish line, Yu Hengzhi, and all the referees determined the rankings. Except for Fudan's Zhang Huiyuan, who was not scored, the rest were announced in order. In total, Fudan scored 32 points and Jinan scored 46 points. Fudan won this year's Jiangda Cross-Country Championship. The list is recorded as follows: (1) Li Qingji (Jinan), (2) Yang Qingxie (Fudan), (3) Lan Shijie (Fudan), (4) Zheng Boyi (Fudan), (5) Chen Tianhe (Jinan), (6) Xu Yongqi (Fudan), (7) Li Zongkun (Fudan), (8) Yao Mutian (Jinan), (9) Peng Lianhao (Jinan), (10) Yao Zhaofu (Fudan), (11) Huang Fuyan (Jinan), (12) Li Congxin (Jinan).

Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

Nanyang Inspection Group of the National Goods Circle

— Yang An

Nanyang is an area where overseas Chinese gather. The vast land, the large population, and the deep wealth are all very long-standing. In addition, the patriotic enthusiasm of the overseas Chinese and the psychology of favoring national goods are indeed the best market for national goods sold abroad. This publication has contributed this idea to the national goods circle more than once over the years, and those who are enthusiastic about national goods among overseas Chinese have also tried their best to promote it. Consul General Song Faxiang of the Dutch East Indies is one of the most enthusiastic people. He spares no effort in advising and guiding. He has discussed and discussed perfect methods several times at the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and the China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperation Association. Recently, he attended the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association and reported on the progress of promoting national goods in the South, and came to Shanghai to solicit products from various factories to participate in the Nanyang National Goods Touring Exhibition, which will open in April next year, in order to expand and develop trade in Nanyang. At the same time, based on the achievements of the Singapore National Goods Exhibition, local overseas Chinese all said that the motherland's industry has made such progress and the products are so sophisticated that everyone expressed their welcome. All the products shipped by various factories were sold out, and there was still a shortage of supply. Therefore, the national goods people who attended listened to Mr. Song's report and unanimously believed that the publicity and contact with Nanyang by various factories should be carried out vigorously at present, because there is an organized action of the Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group. This is a fundamental policy to seek a way out for national goods in response to the needs of the times. The reporter very much hopes that under the guidance of the International Trade Bureau and Consul General Song, it will be completed as soon as possible and go together. As far as the reporter can see, the tasks of this group and this trip should include the following seven points.

(1) Describe the latest situation of the national goods circles in the motherland, and the manufacturing situation of various factories. It is best to bring the industrial films taken by various factories to be screened. The true knowledge and insight are especially impressive.

(2) Investigate the living conditions of overseas Chinese in Nanyang and the items they usually use, and study their psychology and preferences, so that when making products, we can cater to their preferences and suit their application.

(3) Investigate the trends of the Nanyang market and the degree of purchasing power of the general society, so as to determine the steps and policies of trade.

(4) Investigate the currency and exchange situation in Nanyang to determine the standard of prices.

(5) Investigate the transportation procedures in Nanyang and the collection standards of tax regulations, so that the shipment and delivery of goods have a certain calculation, so as not to lose the trust of overseas Chinese.

(6) Contact Nanyang vendors and agree with them on the method of distributing national goods.

(7) Establish a Nanyang National Goods Introduction Office to facilitate the consultation and procurement of overseas Chinese, and to be responsible for domestic and foreign communications at any time.

Recently, the Ministry of Communications has responded to the request of overseas Chinese in Nanyang and is actively planning to open Nanyang routes to facilitate the circulation of national goods. This matter is closely related to the development of Nanyang national goods. Although it currently requires a huge amount of 25 million yuan in expenses, with the patriotic enthusiasm of overseas Chinese and a high degree of certainty in business, it should be implemented as soon as possible.

A Visit to the China Chemical Industry Society

— Quan Jia

On the afternoon of November 27th, at 2 o'clock, we took our visitor's passes from the China Chemical Industry Society, and six of us went together to the factory gate on Pinlang Road in Shanghai. We were greeted by a Mr. Fan, who gave us a very detailed explanation, leaving a very good impression.

We first went to the soap-making room. There were several large pots cooking fat. After it was melted, it was put into a mixer where an alkaline solution was added, and it was continuously stirred to alkalize the fat. This is called soap stock. Ordinary laundry soap is made by cooling this soap stock, putting it in a wooden frame, and stamping it with a trademark. When we went, they were making perfumed soap. The method was to cut the soap bars into thin slices, then move them into an oven to dry them. Then, appropriate pigments and fragrances were added, and after it was completely mixed, it was pressed into long strips. Finally, it was stamped with a trademark in a stamping machine.

In the second part, we went to the toothpaste and cold cream production area. The factory was very clean. The raw materials for toothpaste are sodium carbonate Na2Co3, calcium carbonate CaCo, glycerine (glycerine C3H5(OH)3……CH2(OH)-CH(OH)-CH2(OH)). Auxiliary materials commonly used are gum powder, alcohol (CH7CH2OH), boric acid, syrup, etc. The fragrances used are anise oil, peppermint essence, rose essence, etc. The first step is to refine the gum, gradually heating it. After a suitable amount of time, it is moved into a cream-rolling machine to be rolled until it achieves a sticky, toffee-like consistency. The second step is to fill the cans. This work requires three people. The first person pulls a lever to fill the tin cans with toothpaste. The second person takes it, uses a machine to flatten the bottom of the tube, then rolls the bottom edge, and passes it to the third person, who then adds a bottom clip and fastens it with a machine. This is the product that we buy. The movements are very skilled. We watched for quite a while.

The raw materials for cold cream are stearic acid, sodium carbonate, potassium carbonate, etc. First, they are put into a large pot and heated, while being stirred, until they dissolve into a paste. Then, they are placed in a large lead bucket and stirred manually. At this time, the color and shape are like ordinary paste, not very attractive. Then, when it is half-cooled, fragrance is added, and it is stirred until it is evenly mixed. This is cold cream. The factory's products include "Era Cream," "Fragrant Ze Zhi," and "Three Stars Original Cold Cream," which are very popular on the market.

In addition to the above three types, the factory also produces seasoning powder (the most common on the market are "Wei Sheng" and "Guanyin Powder" (a type)), soy sauce essence, caramel coloring, and mosquito coils, starch, etc. In particular, "Three Stars" mosquito coils are something we come into contact with almost daily in the summer. Their reach has almost extended to small cities and towns across the country, becoming a popular product for the masses. Unfortunately, we did not get to visit all of them, which is a regret.

Before the establishment of the China Chemical Industry Society, foreign goods filled the domestic market. Later, the "Three Stars" brand gradually took over. Except for raw materials that China does not have, which have to be purchased from Germany, the rest are made with domestic products. In recent years, business has developed, and there are two distribution centers in Shanghai. Branches have also been opened in Tianjin, Hangzhou, Nanjing, Qingdao, and other places. The total annual turnover is about three million yuan.

After the visit, we felt extremely satisfied. Finally, we expressed our deep gratitude to Mr. Fan for his enthusiastic hospitality.
