Publishing World

The Demand for Freedom of Speech

— Xing An

In China after the national crisis, the lack of freedom of speech has simply turned it into a silent China. Not only is genuine public opinion unable to be fully expressed, but also the various situations of internal and external affairs are not dared to be fully reported. As a result, the general public is kept in the dark, waiting for national subjugation!

Freedom of speech is inherently permitted by national law. The reason why the authorities have recently taken a monitoring attitude towards speech must have its own unavoidable difficulties. However, suppressing speech should have clear methods, stipulating a certain scope, allowing people the opportunity to express their views. If speech really goes beyond the bounds, then it should be prohibited, which is naturally permissible. If it is simply suppressed across the board, not allowing even correct commentary or truthful news to be published, then it is an excessive oppression. This not only deprives the people of their freedom of speech, but is also detrimental to the country!

Today's China is facing a critical juncture of life and death. To save the country and seek survival, it is necessary for the whole nation to rise up together and jointly face the national crisis. But to get the people to save the country, they should at least be allowed to understand a little about national affairs and express their opinions on national affairs. This cannot be done without opening up speech. Because speech is a powerful intangible weapon, the government's diplomacy is prone to failure without speech as its backing!

At this Fifth Plenary Session, some members of the Central Committee proposed a motion to open up the press and restore freedom of speech, which is extremely necessary. Recently, the Nanjing Central Daily News also published an article asking the authorities to change the news policy, which shows that freedom of speech has become an urgent demand of the people. The editorial conclusion of the newspaper said: "The situation is so serious today that the preliminary and fundamental remedy we have in mind is for the government to quickly change its news policy. The party headquarters or the government agencies in charge of news should quickly discuss with the press a simple method, clearly stipulating a few strict restrictions. Apart from that, all conspiracies and actions and people who endanger the country, all facts and behaviors that poison politics and destroy the principles, the expressions and actions of the people's patriotic behavior, especially the various criticisms of foreign newspapers and the factual records, should all be allowed to be published in domestic newspapers. If this method can be implemented, we believe that after three months, the situation in our internal affairs and diplomacy will be refreshed. At that time, the government will be able to directly and indirectly obtain unexpected strength to assist it in promoting various political undertakings and renewing the political lineup. This is by no means empty talk, nor is it the view of a scholar. We sincerely pray that the authorities adopt this suggestion immediately and hope that the entire press will work together to realize this ideal to serve the country." These words are very insightful!

We guarantee to the authorities here that the people's struggle for freedom of speech is only with good intentions and no malicious intent. The people's demand for freedom of speech is aimed at saving the country and they absolutely do not want to harm the country. Therefore, we hope that the government can be mindful of the difficulties of the times, listen to the people's opinions, and open up speech, so that the people can get an opportunity to serve the country. We also hope that the entire press will rise up and work hard to achieve the goal of realizing freedom of speech!

Reading "A New Land Program for China"

— Zeng Jianping

By Yin Zhenxia, published by Zhengzhong Book Company

Since Yan Xishan announced his land proposal, scholars from all walks of life in the country have suddenly started to discuss this long-idle issue. Obviously, the land issue, no matter when, has always occupied the center of China's governance and chaos for two thousand years, and it is not easily abandoned or avoided.

However, although China's land problem is very important, the general works on this problem in bookstores are very scarce. Because of the scarcity of this type of book published in bookstores, the "Chinese Land System" and "Collection of Studies on Chinese Land," published by Commercial Press, "Research on Chinese Rural Economy," "Research on Chinese Land System," and "Land Tax System of the Two Song Dynasties," published by New Life, and "Ancient Chinese Society" by Liming, and "History of Chinese Land System" by Zhengzhong, etc., have become the main reading materials for young people who generally study China's land problem. At the same time, these readings are mostly about the study of the land system of past dynasties in China, and rarely touch on the issues we are currently arguing about. However, while there is a shortage of these books, fortunately, Mr. Yin Zhenxia's "A New Land Program for China" has been read by the author.

First of all, we must acknowledge that Mr. Yin Zhenxia's work is a book completed with great energy and is a work that clarifies Mr. Sun Yat-sen's fundamental proposition. Because Mr. Chen Lifu said in his preface to it: "The local land program can clarify the way to equal wealth and eliminate the poverty. Reading this, one will be more aware of the greatness of the Principle of People's Livelihood." And Mr. An Ruoding also believes that "After reading it carefully, the book analyzes how to divide the land, how to allocate the population, how to reform the land system, and how to reorganize the land tax... one by one, with practical methods." It can be seen that the book has considerable correctness in its argumentation.

However, although Mr. Yin's work has considerable correctness in principle, the author believes that there are still several points that should be discussed after careful reading. For example:

First: In the second section of the fourth chapter of the book, "The Well-Field System," the author quotes Du You's Tongdian, which says: "In the past, the Yellow Emperor began to manage the land and set up wells to stop disputes, and established steps and acres to prevent shortages, making people's homes into wells, and wells opening four roads... and the system was not changed until Xia and Yin," then unquestioningly asserts: "This is the well-field system of the Yellow Emperor's era. The Yellow Emperor's well-field system adopted large-scale agricultural management, with eight families jointly producing and jointly distributing..." At the same time, he further cites Mencius's saying that "eight families all privately owned 100 acres" and the saying in the Book of Songs that "the rain wets our public fields, and then our private fields," thus concluding that the land system of the Zhou Dynasty changed dramatically from the "public ownership and public management" of the Yellow Emperor to the "public ownership and public management" of the early Zhou Dynasty until the Spring and Autumn Period. We dare not agree with this affirmative attitude.

Because Du You's Tongdian's records about the field system of the Yellow Emperor's era can be said to be completely forged by associating with Mencius's opinions. The unreliability of this material has long been determined by knowledgeable people, and the so-called Yellow Emperor's era was historically the early clan society of China. The common possession of land by clan societies is the first form of private land ownership. Under this form of land ownership, even if the rural commune form is adopted to manage the land at that time, there can never be a system of "eight families" jointly producing and jointly distributing. However, Mr. Yin, in this book, unquestioningly gives an affirmative judgment, which we dare not agree with.

Second: From the Zhou Dynasty to the Spring and Autumn Period, we cannot recognize that the land system at that time was unconditionally "public ownership and private management." Because from the early Zhou Dynasty to the Spring and Autumn Period, Chinese society had gradually moved from a tribal society to a feudal society. The country formed by the feudal landlord aristocracy holding land is the second form of private land ownership. Since the rulers at that time were constantly fighting for land and constantly granting land to their subordinates, how can we determine the existence of the land communal system before the Spring and Autumn Period! Therefore, we cannot agree with Mr. Yin's citation of ancient Chinese field systems, which does not adopt newer theories and research, but only believes in ancient people and ancient books and draws conclusions hastily.

Third: The author made a mistake in the seventh section of the fourth chapter of the book, "Equal Field System." He cited the statement that "men are granted 40 acres of land, called 'double field,' and women are granted 20 acres of land, called 'exposed field.'" This point is inconsistent with the facts. Because the equal field order of the Yuanwei Year 9 clearly stated: "All men over the age of fifteen are granted 40 acres of exposed fields; women are granted 20 acres... The fields granted are generally doubled; fields with three rotations are doubled again to supply cultivation and the increase and decrease in grants." (See Wei Shu Shi Huo Zhi) It can be seen that the 40 acres received by a man at that time were exposed fields, not double fields. The so-called double fields were additional fields outside the mulberry fields and exposed fields at that time. It was increased or decreased according to the quality of the land. Now the author regards the 40 acres received by each man as double fields, which is obviously inconsistent with the facts at that time. This is what the author dares to ask the author to pay attention to.

Fourth: The author also repeats the above-mentioned mistakes in the "Conclusion" of the fifteenth section of the fourth chapter of the book. He said: "Summing up the land systems of the past dynasties mentioned above, generally speaking, they can be divided into five periods: (1) the period of public land ownership and public management, before the three dynasties; (2) the period of public land ownership and private management, from the three dynasties to the end of the Zhou Dynasty; (3) the period of private land ownership, from the Warring States period to the Northern and Southern Dynasties; (4) the period of national land ownership revival, from Emperor Xiaowen of the Later Wei Dynasty to the middle of the Tang Dynasty..." (See page 46 of the book) In my opinion, this conclusion is also not very appropriate. Because the so-called national land ownership is originally the second form of the private land ownership system. The so-called national land ownership from Yuan Wei to Tang is actually the private ownership of the feudal landlord aristocracy at that time, which is completely different from the content of modern so-called national land ownership. The vast land occupied by the nobles and powerful people of the past dynasties at that time, the existence of the manor system of the noble landlords, and the emperor's constant granting of large amounts of land to powerful ministers, all prove that there could not have been any national land ownership system in China from Yuan Wei to Tang, let alone a revival period of national land ownership. In this book, the author opposes this kind of "national land ownership" to "private land ownership," which is obviously a bit incorrect in methodology.

Fifth: At the same time, the author also made a small mistake in the sixth chapter of the second part. That is, after the author cited various statistics to prove the reduction of arable land in the provinces of mainland China, he concluded that "the drastic reduction of farmland and farm households in the five provinces of Yu, E, Xiang, Gan, and Yue is probably affected by A natural disasters, B bandits, C poor governance, and D the decline of the rural economy, resulting in farmers' inability to maintain themselves and escape death, so they abandon their cultivated morning land." (See page 8). Undoubtedly, this conclusion lightly glosses over the fact that the imperialists' aggression against China has deepened China's natural and man-made disasters and created China's political instability, which is the main factor. If it were as the author said, it would easily lead readers to regard the above-mentioned reasons as spontaneous phenomena in China, unrelated to imperialism. Then, wouldn't it be letting go of a major culprit?

Regarding this point, the author hopes that Mr. Yin can correct it in his second edition.

In short, the second part of the book "A New Land Program for China" is better than the first part. Because the first part focuses more on theory, and the second part focuses more on practice. In the sixth chapter and beyond, especially in the reform of rural arable land, the author has given us many practical methods. Therefore, when the problem of China's land system has been forced from theory to practice, this book is still worth reading.

Reading the First Volume of China Post

— Zhuang Xinzai

Written by Zhang Biao Ren, published by Commercial Press

The current Chinese revolution has progressed from the process of shouting to the process of practical work, and the work of destruction needs to be replaced by the work of construction. Needless to say, China is praised by all countries in the world for the various practical achievements created through hard work in recent years: just to say that to make China advance into a modern new country, it is urgent to organize and implement various new undertakings. In the past 100 years, the most concrete manifestation of the Chinese revolution has actually been in the field of transportation, and among the transportation undertakings, the most outstanding achievement is the postal service. Speaking of the postal service, it is as common as clothing, food, housing, and transportation, and maintains a close relationship with people's daily life. Who doesn't know that the postal service is an institution for delivering letters, who doesn't have a direct connection with the postal service, and who doesn't know that the postal service is the best new undertaking run by China. But further ask where the postal service's performance is good? More concerned people will know that the reason why the postal service is praised by China and foreign countries is that its organization is complete and strict, and it can be the most unified administrative organ in the country; the examination of personnel is precise and prudent, and it can be called the most suitable for the spirit of the European and American civil service system: the handling of affairs is quick and reliable, and it is full of a sense of responsibility, which can be called a model for talking about administrative efficiency: and the postal service can really enable the people to obtain the greatest enjoyment with the lowest sacrifice, which can be said to be a new undertaking that is most in line with welfareism. These words are certainly correct, but if you ask further why the Chinese postal service can create such achievements and reputation? I am afraid that no one knows what to say, but how can the outstanding achievements of the postal service be accidental?

In recent years, the Chinese government and the public have known to work hard on the transportation industry, but the substantial advancement of the transportation industry must first make the people have a full knowledge of the transportation industry, so that they can know the way to use it and fulfill the responsibility of loving it. For example, the postal service: in terms of history, the trial has been carried out for more than 60 years, in terms of scope, from large cities to remote and dilapidated areas, covering the whole country: in terms of its relationship with the people, it is the most universal, the most close and important. However, there has been no special work that systematically describes this, so that the people can have a true understanding of it, and understand why the postal service is doing well, that is, the implementation of other new undertakings can also get a good mirror for this, which is really a major regret in the creation of a new country and new undertakings. But now, this regret has been made up for by the publication of Zhang's China Post.

The whole book of China Post has about 500,000 words, divided into three volumes: upper, middle, and lower. The upper volume has been published recently, divided into four parts and 17 chapters, focusing on the administrative department of China Post. After reading it, this book traces the past evolution of the postal service in detail and clearly; the current organization, the vertical subordination, the horizontal connection, and its procurement, operational powers, tasks, all have precise and profound observations, not only superficial analysis and introduction. As for the appointment, salary, performance evaluation, shifts, rewards and punishments, duties, retirement, etc. of personnel, they are described in detail, dissected in depth, and measured with the academic principles of personnel administration to weigh their gains and losses; the final chapter discusses the organization and function of postal personnel groups as its final. Various laws, regulations, and anything related to the postal service are fully equipped. After reading such a great work about the Chinese postal service, I cannot help but think of the considerable energy spent by the author. (To be continued)

Mr. Zhang Liangren, the author of this book, is a PhD in economics from Germany. He has served in transportation and postal administrative agencies for many years after returning to China, and has personally participated in the revision of postal laws and regulations. Naturally, such a specialized work must be written by an author with rich knowledge and experience, in order to take care of both academic theory and facts, integrate and connect them, and avoid the drawbacks of being superficial or dry and shallow.

After reading this book, I had three feelings: First, there is no reason for anything to be lucky. The excellent performance of China's postal service has its own reasons for being excellent. This reason lies in the postal administrative organization, the dynamic and static mechanisms are strict and reasonable, and can operate flexibly within the track. In terms of personnel, the selection, use, and treatment of personnel can enable everyone to make the best use of their talents and devote themselves to the development of public affairs with peace of mind. Second, the achievements of the postal service can be extrapolated to other undertakings, and even to government agencies. If you want to make the operation of the undertaking economical and reasonable, increase efficiency, be responsible, and reduce waste, you must pay attention to the administrative organization mechanism and the appointment and treatment of personnel. Therefore, this book is not only the only systematic classic in the administrative aspect of the Chinese postal service, but also for those who seek to improve management, make operations economical and reasonable, and develop undertakings, as well as those who are concerned about the improvement of administrative agency organization and personnel administration, China Post is the most valuable practical example. Third, I feel that China's publishing industry has great hope for progress, and can gradually move towards more specialized and in-depth research, and no longer limit itself to general introductions to sociology and general discussions of political science, textbook books. From this, I further hope that the publishing industry will have more systematic writings of a more specialized nature that involve all aspects of the new undertakings of this country, which will be of infinite help to the creation of a new China.

The above are just the words I thought of saying after browsing the first volume of China Post. The middle volume focuses on postal business, and the lower volume focuses on postal economics. I hope very much that they can be published as soon as possible to complete the entire canon of the Chinese postal service.

Bookstore Miscellany (Continued)

— Li Hengzhi

(7) Proofreaders

In the editorship of a new bookstore, the reason we mention proofreaders immediately after the editor-in-chief, without mentioning other personnel, is because proofreading is a task that is relatively unnoticed, but in fact, it is quite interesting and important. People in the book industry certainly know what proofreading is all about, but people outside the industry may not know much. So, I must first tell you that proofreading, simply put, is the process of correcting the unedited proofs sent by the printing house, which have been typeset but not yet printed, according to the original manuscript. Isn't this work very simple? As a result, in the early stages of the new book industry, there were just too many interesting things happening in bookstores due to proofreading.

"Proofreading" can be said to be an even more difficult task than "clipping newspapers". Isn't clipping newspapers very easy, what's so difficult about it? But according to the reports of people who have experience with clipping newspapers, no one succeeds at first. For example, first, you must know how to choose and discard materials, and second, you must know how to classify materials. If this kind of work is done by someone without experience, even if you tell him which section of the news to clip, he may only clip the first section and forget the second half published on another page or in another line. Although the situation of proofreading is different, its difficulty is actually the same in principle.

Bookstore owners without experience (or general managers, editors-in-chief, in short, those in charge) think that proofreading is easy, so at first, most of them are unwilling to pay higher wages to hire proofreaders. Some even assign apprentices to do it, resulting in countless errors in new books. Some writers are dissatisfied with other people's proofreading and think that proofreading is easy, so they often ask the bookstore to proofread the manuscripts themselves, but the result is even worse than what the apprentices in the bookstore proofread. Proofreading seems to be somewhat mysterious. People with insufficient academic ability and poor writing skills think that proofreading only requires comparing word by word, so naturally, they will make unimaginable mistakes. On the other hand, even if the original author does the proofreading, he may feel very satisfied when he is proofreading, but after the book is published, there will be mistakes that even he cannot believe. Some even think that the printing house made the mistakes.

Supplement to the Local Edition of Shen Bao

Talk

The American Airplane "China Clipper" Successfully Crosses the Pacific Ocean

— Li Min

Recently, there has been a noteworthy event in the Pacific Ocean: the successful crossing of the Pacific by the American airplane "China Clipper." This plane has four engines, each with 800 horsepower, and a carrying capacity of 51,000 pounds. It took off from Alameda on the west coast of the United States, passed through Honolulu, Midway Island, Wake Island, and Guam, and flew to Manila, Philippines. The entire journey of 8,000 miles took only five days, which can be said to be the first great feat since the advent of transportation in the Pacific. Therefore, the American people have been greatly encouraged and delighted by this event, and countries around the world have also paid great attention to it.

In terms of the benefits of science to mankind, this event is very worthy of praise. The development and utilization of science by mankind is originally aimed at increasing human happiness. Like this time, the "China Clipper" crossed the Pacific Ocean, greatly shortening the originally vast transportation in the Pacific and rapidly promoting the close relationship between the world's people. This is of great benefit to the happiness of the people. Not only is this event so, but in other aspects, such as the use of explosives to open up mines and steep mountain roads, and the use of poison gas for sterilization and other medical and agricultural applications, even the things that people consider the most dangerous are beneficial to mankind as long as the purpose of their use is correct. As for the benefits of airplanes and radios to mankind, it goes without saying. Now, however, they have been innocently used by a small number of selfish people. As a result, everything that was originally beneficial to people has become a poisonous substance harmful to mankind. For example, airplanes are used to drop bombs, explosives and poison gas are used as weapons for large-scale killing, ships can be converted into warships, and radio can be used for military purposes. Marconi, the founding father of radio, has even followed Mussolini to Africa to be his assistant in killing people. These many events show how modern science is being used by some selfish people to harm people. As for the American airplane "China Clipper" crossing the Pacific this time, we have no way of guessing whether the US government's motive is to promote Pacific transportation, but in the midst of preparing for another naval conference, Japan has honestly issued a dissatisfied protest regarding this matter. In the air route of the "China Clipper," we can smell a very strong smell of gunpowder.

Only by standing on the "victim's position and uniting to resist the few selfish people, and taking back all the scientific weapons that are beneficial to mankind from their exclusive poisonous hands, can the people use all science to re-create blessings for the people. And the Chinese people bear the greatest responsibility in this mission. Originally, the Chinese people are now the group of people in the world who are most deeply "victimized." The American large airplane crossing the Pacific Ocean wants to be named "China Clipper," precisely implying this serious meaning.

Memories of the South

— Huang

Every morning, when the autumn wind full of coldness blows into the small building, it often brings a burst of tragic trumpet sounds, occasionally mixed with the sound of hooves and the rustling of orderly footsteps. At this time, my heart also sinks along with it.

"Another person's life is about to end!" I think like this when I hear this ominous sound. Sometimes, I unconsciously walk closer to the front of the building, lean on the railing and look down. Below, there is an orderly line—a flag bearer walks in front, followed by a dozen infantrymen. The snow-white bayonets on their gun barrels shine in the morning sun. Next are the people waiting for execution. Some are sitting in rickshaws, some are sitting in bamboo baskets carried by one or two people, but some are walking on their own. The last in the line is the supervising officer, riding on a small horse.

Some passers-by occasionally stop to watch, but most turn their faces away, unwilling to take a look at these people who only have a few minutes or ten minutes left in this world.

A few years ago, behind such a line, there were often crowds of onlookers, shouting non-stop: "Go watch the shooting! Go watch the shooting!" But now, this scene is rarely seen. Is it out of habit? Or for some other reason? I don't know. However, since the beginning of autumn, during the winter defense season, the sound of trumpets often blows to this small building with the morning breeze.

I am afraid to see those pale faces, I am afraid to see their trembling before death, and I am even more afraid to see those desolate eyes! It is their last glimpse projected towards the world!

Page 16

I am even more afraid to see the people chasing after them and wailing—their parents, brothers, wives, relatives, or friends. The desolate cries of that kind of death separation are heartbreaking to hear.

"May they..." I often want to bless these dead, and if there is a God, I want to pray for them on their behalf, because he is always our compatriot! But I often only recite the three words "May they...", and I can't say the following requests, because they are called bandits and robbers!

Silver Chain

— Cun Yin

Every time I return home, my six-year-old child always pouts and asks: "Dad, what did you bring for me to eat?"

Upon hearing this charming voice, my heart, which has been running around for years, aches. I think: Why don't I have anything for him to eat? — Previously, when I had a job, I often bought biscuits, chocolates, and almond candies for my children to satisfy their appetites. But now? I am poor, I am unemployed; not only can they not eat those sweet biscuits, but they can't even eat their fill for three meals a day!

The three-year-old girl often cries because of hunger. And the six-year-old child often looks at me with a strange expression.

One day, I was silently writing a self-recommendation letter to find a job when the six-year-old child came back with his schoolbag.

"Dad, I'm back," he said to me happily.

"Did you recite your books today?" I asked him casually.

He smiled, nodded, and jumped to his mother.

I continued to write my letter. Suddenly, he came back again. He showed me a face without a smile:

"Why haven't you bought us anything to eat these many days, Dad?"

I smiled bitterly, and I almost shed tears from my bitter smile. I had nothing to answer him, I just smiled bitterly at him, smiled bitterly...

My wife took two biscuits and came in holding the three-year-old girl. She asked if I was hungry. She handed the girl to me and said to me softly:

"Today, I found a gold chain in the drawer of the cabinet!"

"Um, that's silver! That was given to me by my father!... I hesitated. I didn't know what to do with the silver chain that my father gave me.

"Mom, I'm hungry, let me eat those two biscuits!"

So my wife gave the two biscuits to the child who had just returned from school. However, the child leaning in my arms suddenly cried. She shouted:

"I want to eat too... Mom..."

When I heard this hunger turmoil, I raised my head from my hesitation and said to my wife with grief:

"Let me take that silver chain to exchange for money. Anyway, poor people don't have the blessing of keeping souvenirs."

I immediately walked to the cabinet and took out the gold-plated silver chain from the drawer. I thought to myself:

"It can only sustain us for two days at most!"

Foothills of Ma'anshan

— Chen Liang

Suffocating in the heavy carbon dioxide life of the city, one only needs to occasionally smell some grass and soil, and one will feel as relaxed as if drinking soda water. What's more, in the natural scenery of early winter fields with green pine trees, a bay of clear water, and red leaves scattered all over the mountains! The irregular pattern of yellow pebbles and blue broken bricks paved the small path, the intricate pumpkin vines crawled out of the fence, and the wind-fearing vermilion old pumpkins lay under the large leaves, instilling a kind of fulfilling and joyful feeling into the traveler's emotions.

We waved the mountain firewood sticks in our hands, singing beautiful, relaxed, and light-hearted pastoral songs, and walked through the low firewood gate. Behind us, there were countless strange gazes following, following, until we brought the singing over the crescent-shaped ancient stone bridge. Then, from the yellow, dry lips, the astringent words "Shanghai guests!" were uttered, and then, they went back into the low, dilapidated tile house.

Thin white clouds moved slowly on the treetops of the ginkgo trees. The steps of the frustrated are filled with melancholy. Even the white clouds feel bored? People think that you are in the vast and boundless blue sky, and you can freely finish your journey... but you, but you would rather immerse yourself in the cold water flow, letting a few ignorant village children squat on the bank and throw sharp-cornered broken tiles at the water, and even have your cold, quiet face scratched by a group of duck's claws. One piece scatters, and another piece slowly comes over.

Very few can pass over the mountains without changing their shape as a whole. Similarly, in the journey of life, very few can walk to the end without being hindered by the great winds of life, right? Haha, how many travel companions, how many happy unions, have broken up so distressingly before reaching the middle of the journey, broken up. White clouds in the sky above Ma'anshan, the white-haired reeds of old age are also shaking their heads and sighing at you.

The red leaves all over the mountains are blinking their golden eyes and brown eyes in the warm afternoon sun, showing a look of melancholy. Several white and gray pigeons rest on the roof of the ancient temple halfway up the mountain, sometimes flying up and circling on the black ridge before resting down again. They have no intention of flying far away, perhaps they live in that ancient temple. Small birds can't bear to leave their old nests, and I, who am chronically ill with homesickness, can't help but have some feelings of sorrow stirred up by this.

In the garden decorated with temple pagodas, pine trees, canna flowers, variegated chrysanthemums, and bare plum branches, everyone sat down on the green and yellowish lawn, but I alone liked the cold and shady stone bench. They were planning a time to go back and a relatively free train. "Ah, what busy and hurried vulgar people," I cursed my companions secretly. But then I thought again, I was wrong, they all have families outside, unlike me, who is alone, stubbornly using cigarettes to stain the nails that my parents gave me yellow. Why don't I want to go back? It's just that my home is too far away, too far away. I can't leave the prison of life!

Although the sun is so good, it can't shine into my dark and cold heart. I have the melancholy of red leaves and the old age emotions of white reeds... but I am a young man, why not compare myself to those tall and handsome green pine trees? Why not compare myself to that magnificent rock? "Weak! Weak!" This ridicule seems to be coming from the green pine trees and rocks. I really can't stand it. I smoked cigarettes desperately.

Publishing Industry: "Bubble Monthly," edited and published by the Bubble Society, is a small literary publication with substantial content. It includes Sui Ren's "On Literary Criticism," Shen Dan Ying's "In the Dark Night," Ji Ren's "Street," Ding Wei Nan's "This Group," Wan Nai Hong's "Rent," and Lin Hao's "Paradise Lost." The publication is priced at two cents per copy and two jiao for a full year's subscription. A sample copy with postage is two cents. Address: No. 78, Gujia Lane, Beijing Road.

Suzhou Ballad Singing

Xia Hesheng's Three Smiles

Dunben (800) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening: "Widow Visiting the Grave"

Cultivated good fortune to be fortunate for three lifetimes. Married a husband who was perfect in every way. A loving couple like fish and water. A jade girl and a golden boy complete a good deed. A perfect marriage envied by others. With talent, looks, and money. Who can compare with the joy of others? Nothing in the world can compare with this affection. Envy the mandarin ducks, even the immortals are not envious. Just teaching them to enjoy a lifetime of happiness. Unexpectedly, this perfection was resented by heaven. Disaster struck and illness befell. Gods and Buddhas were ineffective, and medicine was useless. Surprisingly, they snatched away the heart's desire. There was no way to grab the ground and call out to the heavens. From then on, I lived alone and sighed in solitude. Cold pillows and blankets saddened the Qing Dynasty. Feelingless and listless facing the curtain. Time passed quickly like a gap in a colt. The spring light in March is clear and bright. Another Qingming easily passed in a year. A sad person faces a sad festival. Feels even more grieved at this good time. Paper money burned everywhere on the tips of the grass. Every family offered wheat rice to mourn the dead. Look at the young widow. Carrying a grass basket to her husband's grave. Dressed in plain white, she looks elegant. The sad and mournful look is captivating. Personally threw the torches to burn. Bowed down to the tomb door. Rolling tears flowed from her eyes. The nightingale voice was soft and gentle. Telling her recent suffering in guarding. The more she cried, the more miserable and sad. The passers-by on the road shed tears together. Every sound is heart-breaking. If the souls in the ground are conscious. Should understand the servant's heart. Not eating fame and false reputation. Only because of not forgetting the old feelings. It's only pitiful. The white bones in the tomb have no spirituality. Never a word to comfort the widow. It teaches him that this hatred is endless and deep.

Na Ruiting's Hairpin Phoenix

Huiling (1380) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening: "Homesickness"

Went to the imperial court for fame. Good to sell talent and learning to the king. Young people enter the path of Qingyun. White-haired parents are desolate in the past. Marriage in the Prime Minister's mansion is not my wish. It only falls. Long departed from my hometown, leaving my hometown behind. Hometown. Who to rely on. Cai is, Zhang Lao. Xiao is also difficult to last long. Going on the road. Wanting to break my heart. Twelve hours thinking of my hometown. Ah, my parents. It's not that the children abandoned their parents. Forgetting the kindness of nurturing once and for all. But poetry and books delayed me. Now regret the shortcut article. Wife is young. Zhao Wuniang. Marriage in February broke the mandarin ducks. Locking up the charming body of the skirt. Why bother to offer delicious food to the venerable hall. Thinking in my heart. So miserable and hurt. Niu's father-in-law is ruthless. Holding my body tight. I should be the one with the name of unfilial piety. Sighing for a long time. Telling the blue sky. Ah, my parents. I don't know if my body is healthy. Wanting to go home but can't. Pitifully looking at my hometown every moment. One day, at Lu Shi, nine turns in my intestines.

Extra Notes

The Broadcasting Weekly, published by the Radio Weekly Society, has released its 36th issue today. It contains special news from the film and broadcasting industries, several interesting articles, and a supplement with the latest combined program schedule of radio stations. A trial copy with postage costs two cents. Send orders to the Society at No. 48, Lane 478, Xin Zha Road, Shanghai, and they will be promptly fulfilled. Orders placed or mailed before the 10th of this month will receive a 20% discount. The annual subscription price is one dollar and twenty cents.

Among singing groups, the Yiming Society has the largest number of members, with a total of twenty-one, including staff.

Miss Lili of the Yiming Society's greatest hobby is chewing bubble gum.

The Shangxue Society will revive its activities.

Movies

Grand Cathay Presents "Break of Hearts"

One of RKO's Great Productions

Actress Katharine Hepburn, known as the "Second Greta Garbo" in Hollywood, has starred in such blockbusters as "Little Women" and "The Little Minister." This poignant and magnificent work, "Break of Hearts," considered a great production by RKO, also stars her. The film tells the story of a female composer and a famous musician's romance, full of love, separation, joy, and sorrow. The lines "Passionate love is often misled by affection, deep love breeds deep resentment" perfectly describe the characters in the play. The role played by Katharine Hepburn in this film is very suitable for her personality, making her performance particularly moving. The costumes are also lavish and magnificent, unmatched by any other film or star. The film is scheduled to premiere at the Grand Cathay today (Thursday).

"The Boatman's Daughter" Continues to be a Hit

Adding Newsreel of Hu Die's Wedding Today

The latest sound film "The Boatman's Daughter" from Mingxing Film Company has been playing to packed houses at the Jincheng Grand Theatre since its premiere. Yesterday, despite the snowfall, the audience remained crowded, proving that the film is truly moving. Some have praised it as Gao Zhanfei and Xu Lai's most successful work to date, and this is no exaggeration. To please the audience, the theater will also be adding a special screening of "Sound Newsreel of Hu Die's Wedding Ceremony" to each show starting today (Thursday). Everything from the various scenes in the ceremony hall to the trivial details in the bridal chamber is captured as much as possible. This is indeed a very interesting gift for the audience of "The Boatman's Daughter."

Mingxing Diary

Gao Zhanfei teases Hu Die in "Brothers," but in "Flowers of Spring," he is teased by Yan Rijian. Constantly switching emotions while filming "Brothers" and then "Flowers of Spring" requires a well-trained actor to handle.

Yan Yuexian plays a flirtatious singer in "Flowers of Spring" who loves to dress up and has countless boyfriends. Later, she falls into prostitution and commits suicide. During the filming of this scene the other day, Yan Yuexian's hand was injured by gunpowder, almost turning fiction into reality.

"Brothers" has a large-scale school set currently under construction, with more than ten scenes scheduled to be filmed there. It is expected that Hu Die's honeymoon vacation will be over by the time the set is completed.

"Flowers of Spring" satirizes the current crop of unethical male and female celebrities. The other day, while filming a scene where Gao Zhanfei played a temporary extra, a certain actress mistook him for the male celebrity she loved and pursued him vigorously, resulting in a humorous situation.

Xie Yunqing's portrayal of a blind man in "Flowers of Spring" is excellent.

Shu Xiuwen plays an old man in "Brothers," taking three hours each time for makeup.

Because Yan Yuewen plays a noble singer in "Flowers of Spring," several new costumes have been specially made for her.

Filming of "Peach Blossom After the Calamity" has been temporarily suspended due to Hu Die's honeymoon. "Love Letter" was filmed on location in western Shanghai the other day.

Yihua News

Difficult Shots in "Triumphant Song"

"Triumphant Song"—is Bu Wancang's latest masterpiece. The main body of the work has already been filmed. All that remains are the levee opening scenes.

But the opening scenes of this historical drama are proving difficult because they require seven or eight hundred actors, all of whom must be shirtless. The reason, needless to say, is related to the plot. But in this cold weather, getting these actors to strip naked to film the scenes is problematic. Therefore, Bu Wancang feels greatly challenged. But the scene must be filmed. Yes, as soon as the weather clears, they will have to grit their teeth and work.

"Wedding Night" Breaks Work Records

Yue Feng's new work, "Wedding Night," which focuses on marital problems, depicts domestic disputes, and analyzes love affairs between young men and women, is being actively pursued with extreme intensity every day. Over eighty percent has now been completed. According to people in the company, it is breaking all previous records in every aspect. Therefore, not only is Yue Feng complaining bitterly, but all the staff members are also complaining endlessly because they have not had a moment's rest.
